Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Exceptions to the Prohibition of Images in Prayer
Details exceptions for small, headless, and non-living images

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying in the presence of images and identify the three exceptions (small, headless, non-living) that remove the dislike.

Core Idea
Small, headless, or non-living images do not make prayer disliked.

Images in the prayer area are disliked in the Hanafi school, but not all images are equal. This lesson unpacks the exceptions that lift the dislike, based on the principle of avoiding resemblance to idol worship. We will also explore the proof from hadith and the school's interpretation that the angels of revelation, not guardian angels, refrain from entering.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The base ruling from Nur al-Idah is that it is makruh tanzih (slightly disliked) to pray in a place where there are images of living beings, because it resembles worship of idols.
2
Understand the proof (dalil)
The hadith 'Angels do not enter a house with a dog or an image' is taken as evidence. The Hanafi school specifies that this refers to angels of revelation, not guardian angels, so the dislike is not severe.
The hadith is ahad (single-narrated), so it yields zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Learn the three exceptions
The dislike is removed for images that are: (1) small and not easily seen, (2) have the head cut off, or (3) are of soulless things like trees.
These exceptions are based on the principle that such images are not normally worshipped.
4
Know the degrees of dislike
If an image is not exempt, the dislike varies: most severe in front of the person praying, then above the head, then right, left, and least severe behind.
If the image is behind the person and facing the qibla, it is not disliked at all according to some sources.
5
Apply the rules to practical cases
Praying with a coin with a small engraving is fine; a large painting of a lion is disliked; a picture of a tree is fine; a statue with the head removed is fine.
The historical example of Daniel's ring shows that even images of animals were considered permissible.

Except if it (the image) is small, or with its head cut off. Images, like a room (ghurfa) and rooms (ghuraf), and you imagined the thing: you represented its form and shape in the mind so it becomes represented. Sometimes 'image' is used to mean 'description', as they say: 'the image of the matter is such' meaning its description. From that is their saying 'the image of the issue' meaning its description is such. And what is made of wood, or gold, or silver, in the form of a human, it is an idol (sanam). If it is made of stone, it is a graven image (wathan). He disliked that because it resembles their worship. And due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Angels do not enter a house that has a dog or an image.' It is said: the intended are the angels of revelation, but the guardians (hafazah) enter with a person in every entry. And it is said: angels of mercy and forgiveness, but the guardians do not leave except at the time of relieving oneself and a man being alone with his wife. Such is in Al-Burhan. He said in Al-Tabyeen: The most severely disliked is that it be in front of the prayer, then above his head, then on his right, then on his left, then behind him. And in Al-Ghayah: If the statue is behind the back and facing the qibla, it is not disliked because it does not resemble worship. And in Al-Jami' al-Saghir, he declared it disliked unconditionally (except if the image is small such that it is not apparent to the one standing when looking at it except with contemplation, like that on a coin, because it is not ordinarily worshipped. And he said in Al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid: If he prays and has dirhams with images of a king on them, there is no harm because this is too small for the eye. End. Al-Zayla'i said: It is narrated that the ring of Abu Hurayra, may Allah be pleased with him, had two flies on it, and the ring of Daniel, peace be upon him, had a lion and a lioness with a man licking them. End. And in Sharh al-Dayri: And between them was a child licking him. When Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, saw it, his eyes welled up. That was because Daniel, peace be upon him, was thrown into a thicket as an infant, so Allah sent a lion to guard him and a lioness to nurse him, and they were licking him. He intended by this engraving to preserve the grace of Allah upon him. And Ibn Abbas had a kanun surrounded by small images. Such is mentioned by Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir. End. And there is abridgment; because he narrated in Al-Nihayah: When Daniel's ring was found in the era of Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, it was found to have a lion and a lioness with a child licking them. That was because it was said to Bukhtanassar: A child will be born at whose hands your destruction will be, so he started killing those born. When Daniel's mother gave birth to him, she threw him into a thicket hoping he would be safe. So Allah sent a lion to guard him and a lioness to nurse him. He engraved it by way of himself to remember Allah's blessing upon him, and Umar gave it to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. By this it is inferred that he used to pray with it. And Allah knows best. (Or) unless the image is large (headless), because it is not worshipped without a head. And the dislikedness is not removed by placing something like a thread between the head and the body, because it is like a ringed bird. (Or) unless it is (of a soulless thing) like a tree, because it is not worshipped. And it has come in Sahih Muslim from Ibn Abbas that he said: If you must do it, then make trees and what has no soul. He said this to a man who came to him and said: I make images, so give me a fatwa about them. He said: Come close to me. He came closer. Then he said: Come close to me. He came closer until he placed his hand on his head and said: I will inform you of what I heard from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, saying: 'Every maker of images is in the Fire. For every image he made, a soul will be created for it, and it will punish him in Hell.' Ibn Abbas said: So if you must do it, make trees and what has no soul. And in Al-Khulasa: If he sees an image in another's house, it is permissible for him to erase it and change it. And in Al-Tafariq: If he demolishes a house decorated with dyes, he guarantees the value of the house and the dyes if they are not images. Such is in Al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, discusses the ruling on praying in a place where there are images (pictures or statues). It begins by defining the term 'surah' (image) and distinguishing between a 'sanam' (idol made of wood/metal) and a 'wathan' (stone idol). The core ruling is that having images in the prayer area is makruh (disliked) because it resembles idol worship and because the Prophet ﷺ said angels do not enter a house with a dog or an image. The commentator clarifies that 'angels' here refer specifically to angels of revelation or mercy, not the guardian angels who always accompany a person except in certain situations. The passage then explains that the degree of dislike varies based on the image's location: most severe in front of the prayer, then above, then right, left, and finally behind. However, the ruling is not absolute; there are exceptions: images that are so small (like on a coin) that they are not easily seen or worshipped, large images with the head cut off (since they are not considered complete objects of worship), and images of things without a soul (like trees). The text also includes a historical account of Daniel's ring with animal engravings, which was used by Umar and given to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. This serves as evidence that such images were not considered problematic for prayer. Finally, the passage cites rulings from later Hanafi authorities (al-Khulasa, al-Tafariq) about destroying images in someone else's house—emphasizing that it is permissible to remove or alter them, with liability for damages if the house is demolished. Throughout, the commentary follows the Hanafi position that the prohibition is not absolute and is based on the principle of avoiding resemblance to idol worship, not on the mere existence of an image.

Key Terms
صورة (surah): An image or depiction, including statues and pictures. In this text, it refers specifically to images of living beings.
صنم (sanam): An idol made of wood, gold, or silver in human form.
وثن (wathan): A stone idol.
ملائكة الوحي (mala'ikat al-wahy): Angels who bring revelation, as opposed to guardian angels (hafazah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following images makes prayer disliked (makruh)?
A) A small coin with a tiny engraving of a king
B) A large painting of a lion with its head intact
C) A statue of a tree
D) A headless statue of a horse

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits (makruh) images of living beings in prayer only if they are large, have heads, and resemble objects of worship; otherwise, they are exempt.

Praying in Front of a Fire: The Hanafi Ruling
States the ruling that praying before a fire is makruh due to resemblance to fire-worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding praying in front of a fire and distinguish between objects whose presence is disliked and those that are not.

Core Idea
Praying facing an open flame resembling worship is makruh; facing non-worshipped sources of light is not.

In this passage, the author of Nur al-Idah addresses a subtle point of prayer etiquette: the presence of a fire, oven, or brazier in front of the worshipper. The ruling hinges not on the presence of light, but on whether that light source resembles an object of worship. Let us examine the ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is praying with a tannur (oven) or kanun (brazier) containing fire or embers in front of the worshipper. The ruling is makruh (disliked).
The text explicitly states 'ikrah' (dislike).
2
Understand the 'illa (cause)
The dislike is due to resemblance to the Magians (Zoroastrians) who worship fire. The presence of an active fire directly in front mimics their act of worship.
The 'illa is essential for analogical reasoning.
3
Recognize the exception
Candles (sham‘), lamps (qindil), and lanterns (siraj) are excluded from the ruling. They are not objects of worship, so the 'illa does not apply.
The text declares this the 'sahih' (correct) view, citing Al-Tajnis.
4
Note the comparison to a headless statue
The author compares a candle to a statue with its head cut off—neither is an object of worship, so the prohibition vanishes.
This analogy illustrates that the 'illa is the potential for worship, not the presence of fire per se.
5
Apply the ruling to new scenarios
Today, this means praying before a traditional fireplace or gas stove with open flames is makruh, but an electric light or heater is not.
The 'illa (resemblance to worship) remains the decisive factor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يكره (أن يكون بين يديه) أي: المصلي (تَنُّورٌ، أو كانُون فيه جَمْرٌ)، لأنه يشبه المجوس في حال عبادتهم لهـا، وفي « التجنيس » يكره أن يصلي إلى كانون، أو إلى تنور فيه نار تتوقد، لأنه يشبه التعبد، ولو صلى إلى شمع، أو إلى قنديل، أو إلى سراج لا يكره، وهو الصحيح؛ لأنه لا يشبه التعبد لأنه لا يعبد، فصار كتمثال مقطوع الرأس انتهى
(And) it is disliked (that there be in front of him), i.e., the one praying, (a tannur, or a kanun containing embers), because it resembles the Magians in their worship of it. And in Al-Tajnis, it is disliked to pray towards a kanun or a tannur with flaming fire because it resembles worship. But if he prays towards a candle, or a lamp (qindil), or a lantern (siraj), it is not disliked, and that is the correct view, because it does not resemble worship since it is not worshipped, so it becomes like a statue with its head cut off. End.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling of praying where there is a fire. The author states that it is makruh (disliked) to pray with a tannur (oven) or kanun (fireplace) containing embers or flames in front of the worshipper. The reason given is that this resembles the practice of the Magians (Zoroastrians) who worship fire. The text then cites Al-Tajnis, which clarifies that the disliked action is specifically when there is a flaming fire, as it directly mimics worship. However, the ruling is not applied to weaker or non-worshipped sources of light such as a candle (sham'), a lamp (qindil), or a lantern (siraj). The author declares this the correct (sahih) opinion, analogizing such lights to a headless statue—since they are not objects of worship, the resemblance to worship is absent. The commentary thus presents a nuanced position: the underlying cause ('illa) of the prohibition is the resemblance to fire-worship, and once that cause is absent, the ruling does not apply.

Key Terms
تنور (tannur): An oven or furnace for baking, often containing fire.
كانون (kanun): A brazier or fireplace for charcoal or fire.
شمع (sham‘): Candle; a source of light from wax and wick.
قنديل (qindil): A lamp, often oil-based.
سراج (siraj): A lantern or bright lamp.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT considered makruh when placed in front of the worshipper?
A) A tannur with burning wood
B) A kanun with glowing embers
C) A candle (sham‘)
D) A flaming fireplace

Key Takeaway
Praying before an open fire that resembles worship is makruh; non-worshipped lights like candles are not disliked.

Prayer in Front of Sleeping People: Conditions for Dislike
Ruling with proof – conditional dislike

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions that trigger dislike when praying in front of sleeping people and explain the proof from the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
Prayer in front of sleepers is disliked only if faces are faced or distraction is feared.

The presence of sleeping people in front of a worshipper can affect the prayer's perfection, but not all situations are equal. The Hanafi school carefully conditions the dislike to avoid unnecessary burden. Let's examine the exact ruling and its basis in the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on praying while sleeping people are in front of the worshipper. The default hukm is makruh tanzih, but only under specific conditions.
Makruh tanzih means slightly disliked, not sinful.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Aisha from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim, where she lay in front of the Prophet while he prayed at night.
This hadith provides evidence that mere presence of a sleeping person does not invalidate or severely dislike the prayer.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet did not object to Aisha's presence, so the dislike cannot be absolute. It is restricted to situations where the sleeper's face is faced or when disturbance is feared.
The hanafi principle: the hadith is used to qualify the general dislike, making it conditional.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may have stricter views. The Hanafi position is moderate, based on the clear hadith.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate and arises from different interpretations of the same evidence.
5
Summarise the Hanafi position
The prayer is valid but disliked if conditions are met; otherwise no dislike. The mufta bihi is the conditional dislike.
The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(أو) يكون بين يديه (قوم نيام) إذا خشي خروج شيء منهم فيضحكـه أو يؤذيه، أو كان إلى وجههم، فالكراهة لمقابلة الصورة، وأما إذا لم يخش شيئاً ولم يـقـابـل وجـهـاً فـلا كراهة، لما في الصحيحين عن عائشة قالت: «كَانَ رَسُولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يُصَلِّي صَلاةَ اللَّيْلِ كُلَّهَا وأَنا معترضة بينه وبينَ القِبْلَةِ، فإذا أَرَادَ أنْ يُوتِرَ أيقظني فأوترتُ )
(Or) there be before him (sleeping people) if he fears that something from them may come out that will make him laugh or harm him, or he is facing their faces. So the dislike is because of facing the image (of a sleeping person). But if he does not fear anything and does not face a face, then there is no dislike, because of what is in the two Sahihs from Aisha, who said: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, used to pray the entire night prayer while I was lying across between him and the qiblah. When he wanted to pray Witr, he would wake me and I would pray Witr.'
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on praying where there are sleeping people in front of the worshipper. The author states that it is makruh to pray when sleeping people are before him, but only under two conditions: first, if he fears that something might happen from them (like movement or sound) that could distract or harm his prayer, and second, if he is facing their faces. The underlying reason for the dislike is that the sleeper's face is like an image that could distract. However, if neither condition applies—i.e., there is no fear of disturbance and he is not facing their faces—then there is no dislike. The proof is the well-known hadith from Aisha, who would lie in front of the Prophet ﷺ while he prayed at night, and he would wake her for Witr. This shows that the mere presence of a sleeping person (or a person) in front of the praying person does not automatically make the prayer disliked, especially if the person is not facing them directly and there is no distraction.

Key Terms
قوم نيام (qawm niyām): Sleeping people; in this context, people who are asleep and lying in front of the one praying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when is it NOT disliked to pray with sleeping people in front?
A) When they are facing the qiblah
B) When you fear they may move
C) When you do not face their faces and fear no disturbance
D) When they are covered with a sheet

Key Takeaway
Prayer in front of sleepers is not inherently disliked; the dislike only applies when facing their faces or fearing disturbance, based on the hadith of Aisha.

Wiping the Forehead from Dust During Prayer
States that wiping dust from the forehead during prayer is makruh unless necessary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default ruling on wiping dust from the forehead during prayer and identify the condition that permits it.

Core Idea
Unnecessary movements in prayer are disliked; necessary ones are permitted.

This passage addresses a common situation during prayer: when dust or sweat accumulates on the forehead. The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between idle wiping and wiping out of genuine need. Understanding this distinction helps maintain the balance between reverence and practicality in salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The passage states that wiping dust from the forehead during prayer is makruh (disliked) when the dust does not cause harm.
Makruh here is makruh tanzih (lightly disliked).
2
Understand the reason (illa)
The ruling is because such wiping is considered 'abath (idle or unnecessary movement) which detracts from the solemnity of prayer.
'Abath is a key concept in Hanafi fiqh for minor actions.
3
Identify the exception
If the dust or grass harms the person or distracts him from the prayer, then wiping it is permissible (la ba'sa) during the prayer and after finishing.
The condition for permission is actual harm or distraction.
4
Apply the principle to similar cases
The passage extends the same ruling to wiping sweat during prayer, indicating a general principle: necessary small movements are allowed, voluntary ones are discouraged.
This is consistent with Hanafi istihsan for ease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يكره (مَسْحُ الجَبْهَةِ من تراب لا يضره في خلال الصَّلاةِ) لأنه نوع عبث، وإذا ضره التراب أو الحشيش، أو شغله عن الصلاة لا بأس بمسحه في الصلاة وبعد الفراغ، وكذا مسح العرق في الصلاة،
(And) it is disliked (wiping the forehead from dust that does not harm him during the prayer) because it is a type of idle activity. But if the dust or grass harms him, or distracts him from the prayer, there is no harm in wiping it during the prayer and after finishing. Similarly, wiping sweat during the prayer.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This short passage addresses the action of wiping dust off the forehead during prayer. The author rules that it is makruh (disliked) to do so when the dust is not causing harm, classifying it as a useless movement ('abath) that detracts from the reverence of prayer. However, if the dust or grass (hashish) is harmful (e.g., causing discomfort) or distracts the worshipper from being fully present in prayer, then there is no harm (la ba’sa) in wiping it, whether during the prayer or after finishing. The same ruling applies to wiping sweat during prayer. This is a clear example of the Hanafi principle that small movements for necessity are allowed, but voluntary unnecessary ones are disliked.

Key Terms
عبث ('abath): Useless or idle action that detracts from the prayer's solemnity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Never, it is always haram

Key Takeaway
Wiping dust from the forehead during prayer is disliked unless it causes harm or distraction, in which case it is permissible.

The Ruling on Habitually Reciting One Surah in Prayer
Ruling on habitually praying only one surah besides al-Fatiha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on specifying a surah in prayer and identify the condition that changes the ruling from disliked to permissible.

Core Idea
Specifying one surah is disliked only if you believe prayer is invalid without it; otherwise it is permissible.

Have you ever known someone who always recites the same surah after al-Fatiha in every prayer? Is that a praiseworthy routine or a blameworthy habit? This passage from Nur al-Idah clarifies the Hanafi position: the ruling depends on the intention and belief behind the practice, not merely on the act itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the general ruling
The passage begins with the act: 'specifying a surah' (ta'yin surah) meaning always reciting one particular surah after al-Fatiha in every prayer. The initial ruling given is that it is disliked (makruh).
Dislike is the default position according to the matn.
2
Understand the reason for dislike
The text states the reason: 'because it involves abandoning the rest' of the Quran. The habit of always reciting the same surah leads to neglecting other surahs, which is contrary to the sunnah of variety in recitation.
Hijr al-baqi (abandoning the rest) is the key legal cause (illa).
3
Analyze al-Tahawi's qualification
Imam al-Tahawi restricts the dislike: it only applies when the person believes that prayer is not valid without that specific surah. This belief is incorrect and makes the practice blameworthy.
Tahawi's view is an important intra-Hanafi refinement, often cited in later fatwa works.
4
Determine the operative ruling based on intention
If the person does not hold that false belief, and the habit is merely for ease (yusr) or to seek blessing (tabarruk) from a surah the Prophet ﷺ often recited, then it is not disliked. Rather, it is good (hasan).
The key distinction is between a rigid ritual based on wrong belief and a personal practice based on convenience or devotion.
5
Apply to examples given in the text
The text gives examples: reciting 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun' and 'Qul huwa Allahu ahad' (al-Ikhlas) regularly. These are commendable because they follow the Prophet's practice.
The examples show that the ruling is context-dependent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يكره (تعيين سورة) غـيـر الفاتحة؛ لأنها متعينة وجوباً أو سنة على ما تقدم (۳)، بحيث ( لا يقرأُ غيرها) أي: غـيـر الـسـورة الـتي عينها، لما فيه من هجر الباقي، إلا أن « الطحاوي رحمه الله تعالى قيد الكراهة بما إذا اعتقد أن الصلاة لا تجوز بغيرها، وأما إذا لم يعتقد ذلك، أو لم تكن ملازمته ( إلا ليُسْرِ عليه، أو تبركاً بقراءة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم) فلا يكره، بل يكون حسناً، كقراءة وسيج وقُلْ يَتأَيُّهَا الْكَفِرُونَ) و الإخلاخ في بأس
(And) it is disliked (to specify a surah) other than al-Fatiha; because al-Fatiha is specified obligatory or sunnah as has preceded, such that (he does not recite other than it), i.e., other than the surah he has specified, because it involves abandoning the rest. Except that al-Tahawi, may Allah have mercy on him, restricted the dislike to when he believes that prayer is not valid without it. But if he does not believe that, or his adherence (is only for his ease, or seeking blessing from the Prophet's recitation), then it is not disliked, rather it is good, like reciting 'Wa-s-saj' and 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun' and 'al-Ikhlas' in it.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of a person who habitually recites only one particular surah after al-Fatiha in prayer, never reciting any other. The author states that this is generally makruh (disliked) because it leads to abandoning the other surahs of the Quran, which is contrary to the sunnah of variety. However, the great Hanafi scholar al-Tahawi qualifies this: the dislike applies only if the person believes that prayer is not valid without that specific surah (a false belief). If he does not hold such a belief, and his practice is merely out of ease or to seek the blessing of reciting what the Prophet ﷺ often recited (like Surat al-Ikhlas or al-Kafirun), then it is not disliked but rather commendable. Thus, the ruling is nuanced: the general prohibition is against rigidity based on a wrong belief, while following a known prophetic practice is praised.

Key Terms
تعيين سورة (ta'yin surah): Designating a specific surah to be recited in every prayer, to the exclusion of others.
هجر الباقي (hajr al-baqi): Abandoning the rest (of the Quran) by persistently neglecting other surahs.
تبرك (tabarruk): Seeking blessing, especially by following the Prophet's practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it NOT disliked to always recite the same surah in prayer?
A) When you believe other surahs are invalid
B) When you do it for ease or blessing
C) When the surah is long
D) When you recite it silently

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on specifying a surah is conditional upon the belief that the prayer is invalid without it; otherwise the practice is permissible, and if done for ease or blessing, it is even commendable.

Sunnah Recitations in the Five Daily Prayers
Compilation of hadiths on the Prophet's recitation in each prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended surahs for each prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
The Prophet's varied recitations provide the basis for Hanafi sunnah recitations: longer for Fajr, medium for Zuhr/Asr, shorter for Maghrib.

This lesson examines the hadith evidence for the recitations the Prophet (ﷺ) performed in the five daily prayers. The Hanafi school uses these narrations to establish sunnah muakkadah recitations, categorized by length: Tiwal al-Mufassal for Fajr, Awsat for Zuhr/Asr, and Qisar for Maghrib. Understanding this evidence helps you follow the Prophet's practice with confidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer and the hadiths cited
For each prayer time (Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha), note the specific narrations provided. Observe which surahs or verse lengths are mentioned.
The author compiles multiple hadiths per prayer to show variety.
2
Recognize the pattern of recitation length
Compare the lengths mentioned: Fajr often had longer surahs (20+ verses), Zuhr/Asr medium, Maghrib short. The Prophet also varied for reasons like a crying child.
The hadith setting a minimum of 20 verses for Fajr is key.
3
Relate to the Hanafi classification of Mufassal
The Hanafi school divides the Mufassal (short surahs from Qaf to end) into Tiwal (long, Qaf to Buruj), Awsat (Buruj to Bayyinah), and Qisar (Bayyinah to Nas). Match these to the prayers.
Tiwal for Fajr, Awsat for Zuhr/Asr, Qisar for Maghrib.
4
Understand that these are sunnah, not wajib
The Hanafi ruling is that reciting these surahs is sunnah muakkadah but not obligatory. Omitting them does not invalidate the prayer but loses reward.
This is based on the dalil being ahad and the Prophet's consistent practice.

Note: To clarify the surahs that the Prophet (ﷺ) recited in the five times prayers as much as possible, I wanted to transmit from Jalal al-Suyuti's compilation - so that those who are keen on emulating him may benefit from it in his book called 'Al-Yanbu''. Among that is what came in Sahih: Al-Tabarani narrated in Al-Awsat with a sound chain that the Prophet (ﷺ) used to recite in Fajr 'Labayn' (?), and in it: he used to recite in Fajr 'Al-Waqi'ah' and similar surahs. And in Al-Bazzar: he prayed Fajr with Surah Al-Rum. And Al-Hakim narrated that he (ﷺ) was on a journey and prayed Fajr and recited therein: 'Qul a'udhu bi rabb al-falaq' and 'Qul a'udhu bi rabb al-nas'. And the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed with them in Fajr the two shortest surahs of the Quran and the briefest. When he finished the prayer, Mu'adh said: O Messenger of Allah, you prayed a prayer like never before! He said: Did you not hear the crying of a boy behind me in the women's row; I wanted to free his mother for him. And Abu Dawood narrated from a man of Juhaynah: that he heard the Messenger of Allah reciting in Fajr 'Idha zulzilati al-ard'. And Muslim narrated that the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed Fajr in Makkah and began Surah Al-Mu'minun until he reached the mention of Harun and Musa and then bowed. And Muslim narrated that he (ﷺ) used to recite in Fajr 'Wal-Qur'an al-majid'. And Al-Tabarani narrated with a good chain from Rifa'ah al-Ansari that the Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'Do not recite in Fajr less than twenty verses, and do not recite in Isha less than ten verses.' End quote. And regarding Zuhr and Asr prayer: from Jabir ibn Samurah: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) used to recite in Zuhr 'Wal-layli idha yaghsha', and in Asr similarly, and in Fajr longer than that. Muslim narrated it. And it is also narrated that he used to recite in Zuhr 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la', and in Fajr with longer than that. And Abu Dawood and Al-Tirmidhi narrated (and he declared it hasan): 'The Prophet (ﷺ) used to recite in Zuhr and Asr 'Wal-sama'i dhat al-buruj' and 'Wal-sama'i wal-tariq' and similar surahs.' And Al-Nasa'i and Ibn Majah narrated with a good chain: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) used to pray Zuhr with us, and we would hear from him verse after verse from Surah Luqman and Al-Dhariyat.' And Al-Hakim narrated and declared it authentic: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) prayed Zuhr, and prostrated, and we thought he recited 'Tanzeel al-Sajdah'. And he used to recite in Zuhr and Asr 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la' and 'Hal ataka hadith al-ghashiyah'. And he prayed with them the noon prayer and raised his voice, reciting 'Wash-shamsi wa duhaha' and 'Wal-layli idha yaghsha', and Ubayy ibn Ka'b said to him: O Messenger of Allah, were you commanded something in this prayer? He said: No, but I wanted to give you time. And regarding Maghrib: it is established from the Prophet (ﷺ) that he recited in Maghrib 'Al-A'raf'. And in Al-Tabarani's Al-Kabir with a sound chain from Abu Ayyub: the Prophet (ﷺ) used to recite in Maghrib Surah Al-Anfal. And Al-Tabarani narrated with a sound chain from Ibn Umar: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) used to recite for them in Maghrib 'Alladhina kafaru wa saddu 'an sabilillahi adalla a'malahum'. And 'The last prayer the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) prayed was Maghrib; he recited in the first rak'ah 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la' and in the second 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun'. Al-Tabarani narrated: he recited in Maghrib 'Wat-tini waz-zaytun'. Al-Tabarani narrated: he recited in Maghrib 'Ha mim al-dukhan'. And the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed Maghrib and recited 'Al-Qari'ah'.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of hadiths on the Sunnah recitations in the five daily prayers. The author, after mentioning a note about Witr and occasional recitation of Sajdah and 'Hal ata' in Fajr of Friday, transmits a collection from Jalal al-Suyuti's 'Al-Yanbu'' to aid those who wish to emulate the Prophet (ﷺ). For Fajr, various narrations show the Prophet recited longer surahs like Al-Waqi'ah, Al-Rum, Al-Falaq, Al-Nas, and sometimes shorter ones for a reason. He also set a minimum of twenty verses for Fajr. For Zuhr and Asr, the Sunnah is medium-length surahs like Al-Layl, Al-A'la, Al-Buruj, Al-Tariq, and occasionally longer ones like Luqman. The Prophet sometimes raised his voice in Zuhr to teach. For Maghrib, the Sunnah is short surahs like Al-A'raf (longer), Al-Anfal, and often Qisar al-Mufassal such as Al-A'la, Al-Kafirun, Al-Ikhlas, Al-Tin, Al-Qari'ah. The Hanafi school uses these hadiths to establish the mustahabb (recommended) recitations: Fajr: Tiwal al-Mufassal (from Qaf to Buruj) or longer; Zuhr and Asr: Awsat al-Mufassal (from Buruj to Bayyinah); Maghrib: Qisar al-Mufassal (from Bayyinah to end). Isha is between Maghrib and Fajr. This passage does not contain Hanafi rulings per se but provides the evidence. The author does not present a dispute; the Hanafi position is derived from these practices.

Key Terms
التأسي (al-ta'assi): Emulating the Prophet (ﷺ) in his actions and recitations as a form of following the Sunnah.
سنة القراءة (sunnat al-qira'ah): The recommended recitation in each prayer based on the Prophet's practice; not obligatory but meritorious.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Ten verses
B) Twenty verses
C) Thirty verses
D) Forty verses

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school derives the sunnah recitations from the Prophet's varied practice, categorizing them by length for each prayer as sunnah muakkadah.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
The Ruling on Omitting the Sutrah in Prayer
States the ruling on omitting sutrah with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on omitting the sutrah in prayer and explain the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Omitting the sutrah is makruh tanzihi, not haram, because the command is interpreted as recommendation.

The sutrah is a screen placed in front of a worshiper to prevent people from passing directly in front. While many Muslims know it is recommended, the exact ruling when someone might pass is nuanced. In this lesson, we examine a passage from a Hanafi commentary that declares the omission as makruh tanzihi and provides a hadith as proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage addresses omitting the sutrah (taking a screen) in a place where passage is expected. The ruling is 'makruh' (disliked). Determine the exact level: makruh tanzihi (disliked but still valid).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Ibn Umar where the Prophet commands praying towards a sutrah and not allowing anyone to pass. Identify the source: narrated by al-Hakim and Ahmad, classified as ahad.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'fal yusalli ila sutrah' is an imperative (amr). In Hanafi usul, amr indicates wujub (obligation) unless a qarinah (contextual evidence) suggests otherwise. Here, the Hanafis interpret the command as recommendatory (istihbab) because other evidences show the sutrah is not obligatory for validity. The second phrase 'wa la yada' ahadan' also commands, but is directed at the passerby.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may consider the sutrah as sunnah mu'akkadah or even obligatory in some contexts. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in the Hanafi school, omission is disliked but prayer remains valid, while others may view it as a lost reward or require repetition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتَرْكُ اتخاذِ سُتْرَةٍ، في محلِّ يُظَنُّ المرور فيه بين يَدَي المصلِّي. وَتكره ترَكُ اتخاذ سُتْرَةٍ في محلَّ يُظَنُّ المرور فيه بين يدي المصلي؛ لما رواه الحاكم وأحمد وغيرهما. عـن ابـن عـمـر قال: قال رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: « إِذَا صَلَّى أحَدُكُمْ فَلْيُصَلِّ إِلَى سُتْرَةٍ، وَلا يَدَعْ أَحَدًا يَمُرُّ بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ » ولأنَّ ترك اتخاذ السترة فيه تسبيب لوقوع المار في الإثم، فلذا أطلقناه عن قيد كونه في الصحراء أو غيرها فقلناه.
And leaving the taking of a sutrah (screen) in a place where passage is expected in front of the worshiper. And it is disliked to leave taking a sutrah in a place where passage is expected in front of the worshiper, because of what was narrated by al-Hakim and Ahmad and others from Ibn Umar who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When one of you prays, let him pray towards a sutrah, and do not let anyone pass in front of him.' And because leaving the taking of the sutrah is a cause for the passerby to fall into sin, therefore we made the ruling general without restriction to the desert or other places, as we have stated.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the sutrah (screen) in prayer. The author states that it is disliked (makruh) to omit taking a sutrah when one expects someone might pass in front of the worshiper. The proof is a hadith from Ibn Umar, where the Prophet commands praying towards a sutrah and not allowing anyone to pass. The Hanafi reasoning adds that leaving the sutrah causes the passerby to sin by passing in front of a worshiper, which is prohibited. The ruling applies generally, whether in the desert or elsewhere, because the harm (tashbib fi al-ithm) is universal. Note that the ruling here is a makruh tanzihi (disliked) rather than haram, as the omission does not invalidate the prayer but is discouraged. The text is from a sharh (commentary) on Nur al-Idah, providing expansion on the original matn.

Key Terms
سُتْرَة (sutrah): Any object placed in front of the worshiper to create a symbolic barrier, preventing people from passing directly in front of the prayer area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on omitting the sutrah (screen) when one expects a person might pass in front of the worshiper?
A) Haram – it invalidates the prayer
B) Makruh tanzihi – disliked but prayer remains valid
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah – recommended but not disliked to omit
D) Wajib – omission requires sajdah al-sahw

Key Takeaway
Omitting the sutrah when passage is expected is makruh tanzihi, not haram, and does not affect prayer validity.

Recommended Dimensions of the Sutrah
Explains the recommended length and thickness of the sutrah based on hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum recommended length and thickness of a sutrah according to the Hanafi school and explain why these dimensions are recommended (sunnah) rather than obligatory.

Core Idea
A sutrah at least a cubit long and finger-thick is recommended, not required; the prayer remains valid without it.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the recommended specifications for a sutrah (a screen placed in front of the worshiper during prayer). The Hanafi school treats these dimensions as sunnah mu'akkadah, meaning they are highly recommended but not obligatory. The evidence comes from hadith comparing the sutrah to the rear part of a camel saddle, interpreted as a cubit, and from the requirement that it be visible to a passerby.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
Determine what a sutrah is and what the ruling is on using it. The text states it is mustahabb (recommended).
Sunnah mu'akkadah is the term used.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
Find the hadith that provide the basis for the dimensions. The key hadith compares the sutrah to the mu'akhkharat al-rahil (rear part of a saddle).
Also, the hadith about an arrow and the statement of Ibn Mas'ud.
3
Determine the recommended length
The hadith is interpreted by Ata as meaning a cubit or more. This gives the minimum length.
A cubit is about 46.6 cm.
4
Determine the recommended thickness
The text states it should be the thickness of a finger, as anything less may not be visible to a passerby.
The hadith about an arrow also supports this minimum.
5
Note the consequence of non-compliance
Using a smaller or no sutrah does not invalidate the prayer; the prayer remains valid but one misses the sunnah reward.
The ruling is sunnah, not wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في اتخاذ السترة ودفع المار بين يدي المصلي
إذا ظنّ المصلي أي مريد الصلاة مروره، أي: المار يٌستحبُّ له أن يَغْرِزَ سترةً، ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: « ليستتر أحدكم ولو بسهم » وفي « السنن» : « إذا صلَّى أحدكم فليصل إلى سترةٍ وَلْيَدْنُ مِنْهَا » انتهى. وَأن تكون طول ذراع فصاعداً لحديث مسلم: «عن عَائِشَة : سُئِلَ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ سَترَةِ المُصَلِّي، فَقَالَ: مِثْلَ مَوْخِرَةِ الرَّحْلِ » - بضم الميم وهمزة ساكنة وكسر الخاء المعجمة : العود الذي في آخر الرحل، تحاذي رأس الراكب في مؤخر البعير، وتشديد الخاء خطأ، قال المطرزي وفسرها عطاء بأنها ذراع فما فوقها ، كما أخرجه أبو داود، وقال : « أيَعْجَرُ أَحَدُكُمْ إِذَا صَلَّى أَنْ يَجْعَلَ أَمَامَهُ مِثْلُ مُؤخرةِ الرَّحْلِ » وفي حديث آخر : « إِذَا وَضَعَ أَحَدُكُمْ بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ مِثْلَ مُؤَخرةِ الرَّحْلِ فَلْيُصَلِّ ولا يُبَالِ بِمُرُورِ مَار » وتكون السترة في غِلَظ الإصبع وذلك أدناه لأن ما دون ذلك ربما [ لا ] يبدو للناظر، فلا يحصل به المقصود، وروى الحاكم مرفوعاً: « اسْتَتِرُوا فِي صَلاتِكُمْ وَلَو بِسَهُم » وقال ابن مسعود: « يجزئ مـــن السترة السهم » وهو يصلح بياناً للطول والغلظ جميعاً، ذكره شمس الأئمة ( السرخسي ).
Chapter on taking the sutrah and repelling the passerby in front of the worshiper. When the worshiper, i.e., the one intending prayer, expects passage, i.e., of a passerby, it is recommended for him to fix a sutrah, and because of the saying of the Prophet: 'Let one of you screen himself even with an arrow.' And in the Sunan: 'When one of you prays, let him pray towards a sutrah and let him draw near to it.' End. And that it should be a cubit long or more, because of the hadith of Muslim from Aisha: 'The Messenger of Allah was asked about the sutrah of the worshiper, and he said: Like the rear part of a saddle.' – with damma on the mim and a sukun on the hamza and kasra on the kha': the stick at the back of the saddle, facing the rider's head at the rear of the camel; strengthening the kha' is a mistake. Al-Mutarrizi said, and Ata interpreted it as a cubit or more, as recorded by Abu Dawud, and he said: 'Is one of you unable, when he prays, to place in front of him something like the rear part of a saddle?' And in another hadith: 'When one of you places in front of him something like the rear part of a saddle, let him pray and not care about the passing of a passerby.' And the sutrah should be the thickness of a finger, and that is its minimum, because anything less than that perhaps does not appear to the observer, so the purpose is not achieved. Al-Hakim narrated marfu': 'Screen yourselves in your prayers, even with an arrow.' And Ibn Mas'ud said: 'An arrow suffices as a sutrah.' And it serves as an explanation for both length and thickness. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned it.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This is a chapter from the commentary on Nur al-Idah detailing the recommended specifications for a sutrah (screen) in prayer. The author begins by stating that it is recommended (mustahabb) for a person intending to pray to place a sutrah if he expects that someone might pass in front of him. The hadith evidence includes the Prophet's command to screen oneself even with an arrow and to draw near to the sutrah. The recommended length is at least a cubit (dhira), based on the hadith comparing the sutrah to the rear part of a saddle (mu'akhkharat al-rahil), which was interpreted by the scholar Ata as a cubit or more. The thickness is recommended to be at least the thickness of a finger, as anything less may not be visible to the person passing, thus failing to serve as a visible barrier. The hadith about screening with an arrow and Ibn Mas'ud's statement that an arrow suffices are used to support both dimensions. The commentary is drawn from the Hanafi tradition, particularly Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, indicating that these are the relied-upon dimensions. Note that these are recommendations (sunnah), not obligations; using a smaller sutrah does not invalidate the prayer but may reduce the reward.

Key Terms
مَوْخِرَة الرَّحْل (mawkhirat al-rahil): The curved wooden piece at the back of a camel saddle, which the rider's back rests against. Here it is used as a comparison for the size of the sutrah (about a cubit).
ذِرَاع (dhira'): A unit of length, approximately 46.656 cm (based on 6 fist-widths). In this context, it is the minimum recommended length for a sutrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum recommended thickness of a sutrah?
A) The thickness of a finger
B) The thickness of an arrow
C) The thickness of a cubit
D) There is no minimum thickness

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends a sutrah at least a cubit long and a finger thick, but this is sunnah, not obligatory; using a smaller sutrah or none at all does not invalidate the prayer.

The Sutrah for Prayer: Ruling, Dimensions, and the Line Dispute
Commentary on sutrah dimensions, placement, and line ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sutrah, identify its recommended dimensions, and explain the intra-madhhab dispute regarding drawing a line.

Core Idea
The sutrah is a sunnah requiring a physical barrier; a line cannot substitute.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the recommended sutrah (barrier) for prayer. We will learn the evidence for its length and thickness, the proper placement, and the key dispute among later Hanafi scholars: whether drawing a line on the ground can fulfill the sunnah. The relied-upon position maintains that a physical object is essential.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that planting a sutrah is mustahabb (sunnah mu'akkadah) when one fears a passerby. Identify the hukm level and the condition that triggers the recommendation.
The hukm is sunnah, not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith that support the recommendation and the minimum dimensions. Key evidence: 'Let one of you screen himself, even with an arrow' and the comparison to the rear saddle of a camel (mu'khirat al-rahil).
Multiple hadith are cited; note their sources.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the command 'liyastatir' indicates recommendation (nadb) rather than obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. Also, how the hadith on dimensions (forearm length, finger thickness) is derived.
The imperative is interpreted as nadb due to other evidence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on line drawing
Identify the difference of opinion: earlier scholars (including Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) rejected the line; some later scholars (including Imam Muhammad) permitted it. Understand the basis for each view.
The mufta bihi view is that a line is not a sunnah sutrah.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Understand why the preferred view is that a line does not fulfill the sunnah: it does not achieve the purpose of preventing passage. However, drawing a line may be done as a permissible act for spiritual benefit.
Authority: al-Deeri, al-Kamal ibn al-Humam.

Chapter on taking a sutrah and repelling a passerby in front of the prayer. When he fears someone passing, it is recommended for him to plant a sutrah, which should be a forearm in length or more, and the thickness of a finger. The sunnah is to be close to it, and to place it on the side of one of his eyebrows, and not to face it directly. If he does not find something to erect, let him draw a line lengthwise. They also said breadthwise, like a crescent.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn's rulings on the sutrah (barrier) for prayer. It opens by stating the recommendation (istihbab) for a person who expects a passerby to plant a sutrah. The evidence includes hadith: 'Let one of you screen himself, even with an arrow' and 'When one of you prays, let him pray facing a sutrah and be close to it.' The sutrah's minimum length is a forearm, based on the hadith comparing it to the rear saddle of a camel (mu'khirat al-rahil), which Ata interpreted as a forearm or more. Its minimum thickness is a finger, because anything thinner may not be visible to the passerby, defeating the purpose. The sunnah is to be close to the sutrah (so the devil does not cut off the prayer) and to place it aligned with one of the eyebrows (right or left), not directly facing it—the Prophet would incline to one side. If one cannot erect an object, there is a difference of opinion on drawing a line: earlier scholars prohibited it, later scholars permitted it based on a hadith. However, the relied-upon position (al-mukhtar) is that the line is not considered a sunnah sutrah because it does not achieve the objective of preventing passage; it may be done as a pious practice. If drawing a line, it should be lengthwise (like a planted stick) or breadthwise (like a crescent). Imam Abu Hanifa and some others hold that drawing a line or placing a whip does not count as a sunnah sutrah; one must erect something similar to the rear saddle.

Key Terms
السترة (al-sutrah): An object placed in front of the praying person to prevent passersby from crossing and to focus the mind.
موخرة الرحل (mu'khirat al-rahil): The rear wooden piece of a camel saddle, used as a measure for sutrah length (approx. a forearm).
الخط (al-khatt): A line drawn on the ground as a substitute for a physical sutrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on drawing a line as a sutrah when no object is available?
A) It is a sunnah and fully substitutes for a physical sutrah.
B) It is not considered a sunnah sutrah and does not fulfill the recommended practice.
C) It is obligatory to draw a line.
D) It is permissible only if the line is curved like a crescent.

Key Takeaway
A physical sutrah of at least a forearm's length and finger thickness is sunnah; a drawn line does not suffice.

Ruling on Pushing Away a Passer-by During Prayer
States the ruling on repelling a passer-by during prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repelling a passer-by during prayer and apply it by distinguishing between the recommended action and the permissible dispensation.

Core Idea
Leave the passer; only gesture or tasbih as a dispensation.

In this lesson, we examine the rulings related to a person passing in front of a worshiper during prayer. The core teaching is that the recommended action is to remain still and avoid any disturbance. However, a dispensation allows a minimal gesture or a verbal glorification (tasbih) to alert the passer. This delicate balance between maintaining the sanctity of prayer and addressing an unavoidable interruption reflects the Hanafi school's nuanced approach to prayer etiquette.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The passage states the recommended (mustahab) action when a passer crosses in front of the worshiper. First, note that 'mustahab' means doing it is rewarded but not required. What is the recommended thing?
The text says: 'المستحب ترك دفع المار' - the recommended thing is to leave pushing.
2
Understand the dispensation (rukhsah)
A dispensation is given to push away with a gesture (isharah) or by saying 'Subhanallah' (tasbih). This is a concession, not the default. Why is it a dispensation?
Because prayer is built on tranquility, any extra movement is normally discouraged.
3
Examine the evidence (dalil)
The passage cites the Prophet's (pbuh) action with the children of Umm Salamah and the hadith 'When something happens in prayer, let him glorify.' Identify how these evidences support the ruling.
The Prophet gestured to stop the boy but did not speak. The hadith commands tasbih, indicating permissibility.
4
Distinguish between the recommended and the permissible
The recommended is to do nothing. The permissible (rukhsah) is to gesture or say tasbih. What is not recommended? Pushing with the hand is considered makruh (disliked).
The common misunderstanding is that one must push; the text clarifies otherwise.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Think of a real situation: you are in prayer and someone crosses in front. What should you do? First, try to ignore. If necessary, gesture or say 'Subhanallah'. Do not wave arms or speak.
This shows the practical application of the rukhsah.

Source Text

(وَ) إذا اتخذ سترة، أو لم يتخذ، فمر مار بين يدي المصلي، كــان ( المستحَبُّ تَرْكُ دَفْعِ المار)؛ لأن مبنى الصلاة على السكون، والأمــر بـالدرء في الحديث لبيــان الرخصة، كالأمر بقتل الأسودين في الصلاة ) ، (وَرُخُصَ دَفْعُهُ) أي: المار (بالإشارة) بالرأس أو العين أو غيرهما، كما فعل النبي بولدي أمّ سلمةَ حَيْثُ كَانَ يُصَلِّي فِي بَيْتِهَا، فَقَامَ وَلَدُهَا عميرة ليمر بين يديه، فَأَشَارَ إِليهِ أَنْ قِفْ فَوَقَفَ، ثُمَّ قَامَتْ بِنْتُهَا زَيْنَبَ لِتَمُرَّ بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ، فَأَشَارَ إِلَيْهَا أَنْ قِفِـي فَابَتْ ومَرَّتْ، فَلَمَّا فَرَغَ عليه الصلاة والسلام مِنْ صَلاتِهِ نَظرَ إليها وقال: نَاقِصَاتُ العَقْلِ نَاقِصَاتٍ الدين، صواحب يوسف صواحب كرسف)، يغلبن الكرام ويغلبهنَّ اللقَامُ » . (أو) يدفعه (بالتسبيح) لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « إِذَا نَابَ أَحَدُكُمْ نَائِبَةٌ فِي الصَّلاةِ فَلْيُسَبِّحْ ) .
And the recommended thing is to leave pushing away the passer-by. And he was given dispensation to push him away with a gesture or by glorifying (tasbih). And this is the preferred view, as stated in al-Tajnis: When planting the sutra is difficult, throwing (an object) is not considered; that is the preferred view. And whoever considers throwing says: he throws before him lengthwise to make it as if it were planted then fell; this is chosen by Faqih Abu Ja'far. Hisham said: I performed Hajj with Abu Yusuf and he used to throw his whip before him. Thus in al-Taqrib. And because it may make the place a boundary for the prayer, thus the objective is achieved, but he places it lengthwise not widthwise, said Shaykh al-Islam known as Khawahir Zadeh. And there is no harm in leaving the sutra if one is safe from passing traffic and does not face the road, because of Ibn Abbas's narration that the Prophet (pbuh) prayed in an open space with nothing before him. And the sutra of the imam is a sutra for those behind him, because the Prophet (pbuh) prayed in al-Abtah towards a spear that was planted for him, and the people had no sutra. al-Anazah: a staff with a pointed iron tip; the pointed tip is the iron at the bottom of the spear. It is with tanwin (indefinite) because it is a common noun. In al-Kafi, if intended by it the spear of the Prophet, it would be non-declinable due to proper noun and femininity, thus in the accusative. So in al-Inayah. And if he adopts a sutra, or does not adopt one, and a passer passes in front of the worshiper, the recommended thing is to leave pushing away the passer, because the basis of prayer is tranquility, and the command to push away in the hadith is to indicate a dispensation, like the command to kill the two black ones (snake and scorpion) during prayer. And it is permitted to push him away with a gesture—with the head, eye, or other—as the Prophet (pbuh) did with the children of Umm Salamah when he was praying in her house: her son Umayrah stood to pass before him, so he gestured to him to stop, and he stopped. Then her daughter Zaynab stood to pass before him, so he gestured to her to stop, but she refused and passed. When he finished his prayer, he looked at her and said: 'Women of deficient intellect and religion, companions of Yusuf, companions of Karsaf, they overcome the noble and are overcome by the ungrateful.' Or he pushes him away with tasbih, because of his saying: 'When something happens to one of you in prayer, let him glorify.'
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage continues from the previous lesson and now addresses the ruling on a passer-by who crosses in front of a worshiper during prayer. The base matn states that it is mustahab (recommended) not to push away the passer, but a dispensation (rukhsah) is given to indicate with a gesture or by saying subhanallah (tasbih). The commentator explains the rationale: prayer is built on stillness and calm, so pushing is contrary to its spirit. The hadith command to repulse (such as killing a snake or scorpion) is interpreted as a dispensation, not a requirement. The recommended action is to refrain from any action. However, if one does push, it should be by a gesture (like raising the hand or moving the head) or by tasbih, not by substantial movement. The commentator cites the incident of the Prophet (pbuh) with the children of Umm Salamah: he gestured to stop the boy, but the girl passed despite his gesture, after which he commented on women's nature. This shows the permissibility of gestures. Also, the hadith 'if something happens in prayer, let him glorify' (for men) or clap (for women) supports using tasbih to alert the passer. The earlier part of the passage reiterates the line dispute and the permissibility of leaving the sutra if safe, but this is a continuation from the previous lesson and the main new ruling here is on pushing away the passer.

Key Terms
المستحب (al-mustahab): A recommended act; doing it is rewarded, omitting it is not sinful.
الرخصة (al-rukhsah): A dispensation or concession; an act that becomes permissible due to necessity or difficulty, even if normally not allowed.
الإشارة (al-isharah): A gesture, such as moving the head, hand, or eyes, to communicate without speaking or making significant movement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended action (mustahab) when a person passes in front of a worshiper during prayer, according to the Hanafi school?
A) Push the passer away with your hand.
B) Leave pushing and do nothing.
C) Say 'Stop' loudly.
D) Step forward to block the passer.

Key Takeaway
The recommended action is to remain still; if needed, a minimal gesture or tasbih is permitted, but pushing with the hand is disliked.

Repelling a Passer-by During Prayer: Method and Abrogation
Explains the method of repelling a passer-by and abrogation of fighting hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repelling a passer-by during prayer and explain the abrogation of the fighting hadith.

Core Idea
Fighting a passer-by in prayer is abrogated; men use voice, women gesture.

What should a praying person do when someone walks in front of them? In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi position on repelling a passer-by during salah. The text from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies the recommended methods for men and women, and addresses a challenging hadith that seems to permit fighting. By understanding the abrogation (naskh) of this ruling, you will see how the Hanafi school prioritizes the integrity of prayer over confrontation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The text rules on the method of repelling a passer-by (al-mār) during prayer. First, note that combining gesture and verbal glorification (tasbih) is disliked (makruh tanzih) because one suffices.
The dislike is for combining, not for the individual actions.
2
State the methods for men and women
For a man, the recommended method is to raise his voice in Quranic recitation. For a woman, she should use a gesture or clap the back of her right fingers on her left palm; she must not raise her voice.
Women avoid vocal alarm due to fitnah.
3
Analyze the hadith on fighting
The text quotes the hadith: 'When one of you prays... if he refuses, fight him.' This seems to allow physical force. However, the Hanafi school interprets it as abrogated.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
4
Understand the abrogation (naskh)
The ruling permitting actions that break the prayer (like fighting) was from the early period when such actions were permissible. Later, the prohibition of extraneous actions in prayer was established, abrogating this permission.
This is supported by al-Sarakhsi and others.
5
Derive the operative ruling
The operative (mufta bihi) ruling is that a praying person must not fight a passer-by. If a gesture or raised voice does not suffice, the prayer is not invalidated by the passer-by; the person should continue praying.
The prayer remains valid as long as no prohibitive action occurs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(وكره الجمع بينهما)، أي: بين الإشارة والتسبيح؛ لأن بأحدهما كفاية، كذا في «العتابية» (ويدفعه) أي: الرجل يدفع المار إن شاء (برفع الصوت بالقراءة)، كذا زاده الولوالجي، قال صاحب «البحر»: وينبغي أن يكون محله في الصلاة الجهرية فيما يجهر فيه انتهى. وقد يقال: بل في السرية؛ لأن الجهر حاصل في الجهرية، إلا أن يراد به زيادة الجهر، وتدفعه المرأة بالإشارة، أو التصفيق بظهر أصابع يدها اليمنى على صفحة كف اليسرى؛ لأن لهن التصفيق، (ولا ترفع صوتها) بالقراءة أو التسبيح؛ لأنه فتنة، فلا يطلب منهن التسبيح للدرء، ولا يقاتل المصلي المار بين يديه، (وما ورد به) من قوله: (إذا كان أحدكم يصلي، فلا يدع أحدا يمر بين يديه، وليدرأ ما استطاع، فإن أبى فليقاتله، إنما هو شيطان) قال الشيخ أبو سليمان الخطابي: إن الشيطان هو الذي يحمله على ذلك، فهو (مؤول بأنه كان في ابتداء الأمر، والعمل) المنافي للصلاة (مباح) في الصلاة إذ ذاك، (وقد نسخ) كذا قال شمس الأئمة السرخسي رحمه الله تعالى، وما ورد في المقاتلة محمول على الابتداء كان العمل مباحاً فيها، كذا في «شرح الديري» والله أعلم.
And combining them (i.e., gesture and glorification) is disliked. And he (the man) repels it (the passer-by) by raising the voice in recitation, and she (the woman) repels it by gesture or by clapping the back of the right fingers on the palm of the left hand, and she does not raise her voice, because it is a source of temptation. And the praying person does not fight the passer-by, and what is reported about it is interpreted that it was at the beginning when action (in prayer) was permissible, and it has been abrogated. (And combining them is disliked), i.e., between gesture and glorification; because one of them suffices, as in al-Atabiyya. (And he repels it) i.e., the man repels the passer-by if he wishes (by raising the voice in recitation), as added by al-Walwaliji. The author of al-Bahr said: It should be in the audible prayer regarding what is recited aloud, end. It may be said: Rather in the silent prayer, because raising the voice is already present in the audible prayer, unless what is meant is extra raising. And she (the woman) repels it by gesture or by clapping the back of the fingers of her right hand on the palm of her left hand, because for them is clapping. (And she does not raise her voice) in recitation or glorification, because it is a source of temptation, so they are not required to use glorification for repelling. And the praying person does not fight the passer-by between his hands. (And what is reported about it) from his saying: (When one of you prays, do not let anyone pass between his hands, and let him repel as much as he can, and if he refuses then let him fight him, for he is a devil.) Shaykh Abu Sulayman al-Khattabi said: The devil is what drives him to that, so it is (interpreted that it was at the beginning of the matter, and action) that is contrary to prayer (was permissible) in prayer at that time, (and it has been abrogated). Thus said Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, may Allah have mercy on him. And what is reported about fighting is applied to the beginning when action was permissible in it, as in Sharh al-Dayri, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) from the Hanafi school, specifically from Sharh Nur al-Idah (Imdad al-Fattah). It discusses the method of repelling a passer-by during prayer (salah) and addresses the hadith that seems to allow fighting. The text first states that combining both gesture and verbal glorification (tashih) to repel a passer-by is disliked (makruh) because one method suffices. For a man, the recommended method is to raise his voice in recitation (to alert the passer-by without breaking the prayer). For a woman, she should use gesture or clap the back of her right fingers on the palm of her left hand, as clapping is prescribed for women; she should not raise her voice in recitation or glorification because her voice may be a source of fitnah (temptation). The text then clarifies that the praying person should not physically fight the passer-by, despite the hadith that says 'If he refuses, fight him, for he is a devil.' This hadith is interpreted (mu'awwal) as being from the early period of Islam when actions that are now prohibited (like speaking or moving excessively) were still permissible in prayer. This ruling was later abrogated (naskh) by the consensus on the prohibition of such actions. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah as transmitted through the commentary of al-Sarakhsi and al-Dayri.

Key Terms
المار (al-mār): A person who passes directly in front of a praying person, between him and his qibla.
التسبيح (al-tasbīḥ): Saying 'Subhanallah' aloud to alert a passer-by.
التصفيق (al-taṣfīq): Clapping the back of the right fingers on the palm of the left hand.
رفع الصوت بالقراءة (rafʿ al-ṣawt bil-qirāʾa): Raising the voice in Quranic recitation to alert a passer-by.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) By saying 'Subhanallah' aloud
B) By raising his voice in Quranic recitation
C) By clapping his hands
D) By physically fighting the passer-by

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits fighting a passer-by during prayer, relying on abrogation; men should raise their voice and women should clap.

Actions Not Disliked During Prayer: Permitted Secondary Acts
List of actions not disliked during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the specific actions that are not disliked during prayer and state the condition that keeps each permissible.

Core Idea
Many secondary acts are permitted in prayer as long as they do not distract or imitate non-Muslim worship.

The Hanafi school recognizes that a worshipper may need to adjust clothing, be aware of surroundings, or carry a weapon. This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates acts that are explicitly not disliked (makruh) during salah, detailing the conditions that preserve their permissibility. Understanding these rulings helps avoid unnecessary strictness and misconception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Actions
Read through the passage and list each action mentioned as not disliked. There are seven distinct items: tightening the waist, wearing a sword if not distracted, not inserting hands into the farji garment, facing a mushaf or hanging sword, facing the back of a seated speaker, facing a candle/lamp, and prostrating on a carpet with images not prostrated on.
2
Note the Conditions
For each action, identify the condition that removes dislike. For example, wearing a sword is not disliked only if the movement does not preoccupy the worshipper. Prostrating on an image-bearing carpet is not disliked if one does not prostrate directly on the images.
The condition is often 'lack of distraction' or 'not resembling worship of other faiths.'
3
Recognize Intra-Madhhab Differences
Some rulings, like tightening the waist, have a minority view that it is disliked due to imitation of non-Muslims. The passage adopts the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position that it is not disliked. Note which views are chosen (al-mukhtar, al-sahih).
The chosen opinion (al-mukhtar) is the authoritative position.
4
Understand the Rationale
The core principle is that an act is disliked only if it distracts the heart or imitates the worship of other religions. Acts that facilitate worship (like adjusting clothing) or are neutral (like facing a lamp) are permissible.
This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on the intention and state of mind.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما لا يكره للمصلي من الأفعال
لا يُكْرَهُ له شد الوسَطِ. ولا تَقَلَّد بسيف ونحوه، إذا لم يشتغل بحركته. ولا عَدَمُ إِدْخَالِ يديهِ فِي فَرْجِيَّهِ وشقه، على المختار ولا التَّوَجُهُ لمصحف، أو سيف معلّق، أو ظهر قاعد يتحدث. أوْ شَمْع، أو سراج، على الصحيح. والسجود على بساط فيه تصاوير ، لم يَسْجُدْ عليها . .
فصل فيما لا يكره للمصلي من الأفعال
( لا يُكْرَهُ له شدُّ الوسَطِ لعدم شغل البال به كذا في «البرهان»، وفـيـه تشمير لعبادة ربه، فـلا يكره، كذا في « البزازية»، وفي شرح المنية عن الفقيه أبي جعفر الهندوانـــي أنـه كـان يقول: إذا صلى مع القباء)، وهو غير مشدود الوسط، فهو مسيء انتهى. وكذا في ( الخلاصة» ونقل في « البحر » عن «الغياثية» : يكره لأنه صنيع أهل الكتاب، (ولا) يكره ( تقلد) المصلي (بسيف ونحوه إذا لم يشتغل بحركته)، وإن شغله كره إن لم يحتج إلى حمله، كما في ( البرهان»، (ولا) يكره (عَدَمُ إِدْخَالِ يديهِ في فَرْجِيَّهِ وشِقِّهِ ، على المختار)، وكذا في « الخلاصة»، و « البزازيــة»؛ لـعـدم شــغـل الـبـال بـهـا، (ولا ) يكره ( التَّوَجُهُ لمصحف، أو سيف معلّق لأنهما لا يعبدان، ومن الناس من كره ذلك، قلنا: أمـا المصحف فأهل الكتاب يفعلونه للقراءة منه، وهو مكروه عندنا بل مفسد على ما قدمناه، وكلامنا في مجرد كونه أمام المصلي، فلا يكون تشبيهاً بهم، وأما السيف فقد قال تعالى: ﴿وَلْيَأْخُذُوا أَسْلِحَتَهُمْ﴾ [النساء : ١٠٢]، وإذا كان السيف معلقاً بين يديه كان أمكن لأخذه إذا احتاج إليه، فلا يوجـب الكـراهـة، » وَقَدْ كَانَتِ العَنْزَةُ تركز بين يدي النبي ﷺ، فيُصَلِّي إليها، وهو سلاح كما قدمناه )، (أو ظهر قاعد يتحدث في المختار، لقول نافع: «كَانَ ابْنَ عُمَر إذا لَمْ يَجِدْ سَبِيلاً إلى سَارِيَةٍ قَالَ لِي: ول بِظَهْرِكَ » )، (أو شمع. أو سراج على الصحيح؛ لأنه لا يشبه التعبد؛ لأن المجوس لا يعبدون مثل هذا، بل إذا كانت النار مضرمة ، كما في غاية البيان » و « التجنيس » و « البرهان»، وفي « البحر ) قال ابن قتيبة في أدب الكاتب في باب ما جاء فيه لغتان استعمل الناس أضعفهما: الشمع بالسكون، والأوجه فتح الميم، (ولا) يكره ( السجود على بساط فيه تصاوير) ذي روح (لم يَسْجُدْ عليها)، وهذه رواية ( الجامع الصغير ) لأنه استهانة لها، لأنها تداس وتوطأ بالأرجل فلا يكره، كما إذا كانت الوسادة ملقاة، بخلاف ما إذا كانت الوسادة منصوبة، أو كانت الصورة على الستر؛ لأنـه
Chapter on what is not disliked for the praying person from actions: It is not disliked for him to tighten his waist (belt). Nor to wear a sword or similar, if he is not occupied by its movement. Nor not inserting his hands into his farji and shiqq, on the chosen opinion. Nor facing a mushaf, or a hanging sword, or the back of a seated person talking. Or a candle, or a lamp, on the correct opinion. And prostrating on a carpet with images, not prostrating on them. Chapter on what is not disliked for the praying person from actions: (It is not disliked for him to tighten his waist because it does not preoccupy the mind, as in al-Burhan; and in it is tucking up for the worship of his Lord, so it is not disliked, as in al-Bazzaziyah. And in Sharh al-Munyah from al-Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani that he used to say: If he prays with a qaba' (cloak) that is not tightened at the waist, he is doing wrong, end. Similarly in al-Khulasah. And it is narrated in al-Bahr from al-Ghiyathiyah: it is disliked because it is the practice of the People of the Book. (Nor) is it disliked for the worshipper (to wear a sword or similar if he is not occupied by its movement); and if it occupies him, it is disliked if he does not need to carry it, as in al-Burhan. (Nor) is it disliked (not inserting his hands into his farji and shiqq, on the chosen opinion), similarly in al-Khulasah and al-Bazzaziyah, because it does not preoccupy the mind. (Nor) is it disliked (facing a mushaf, or a hanging sword because they are not worshipped; and some people disliked that. We say: As for the mushaf, the People of the Book do that for recitation from it, and it is disliked for us, rather invalidating as we have stated before; and our discussion is merely about it being in front of the worshipper, so it is not imitation of them. As for the sword, Allah Almighty said: 'And let them take their weapons' [al-Nisa: 102]; if the sword is hanging before him, it is more possible for him to take it if he needs it, so it does not entail dislike. And the 'anzah (short spear) used to be fixed before the Prophet ﷺ and he prayed towards it, and it is a weapon as we have stated.) (Or the back of a seated person talking, on the chosen opinion, because of the statement of Nafi': 'Ibn Umar, when he could not find a pillar, said to me: Turn your back to me.') (Or a candle, or a lamp, on the correct opinion, because it does not resemble worship; the Magians do not worship such things, only the fire when kindled, as in Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Tajnis, and al-Burhan. And in al-Bahr, Ibn Qutaybah said in Adab al-Katib in the chapter on words with two pronunciations that people used the weaker one: al-sham' with sukun; the more correct is with fath on the mim.) (Nor) is it disliked (prostrating on a carpet with images) of animate beings (if he does not prostrate on them). This is the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir because it is a contempt for them, as they are trampled and trodden underfoot, so it is not disliked, like if the cushion is thrown down, unlike if the cushion is upright or the image is on a curtain, because...
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement listing actions that are not disliked (makruh) for a person engaged in salah. The Hanafi school provides specific permissions based on necessity and lack of distraction. The text mentions: (1) Tightening the waist (e.g., wearing a belt or sash) is not disliked because it does not preoccupy the mind and is considered tidying up for worship, though some reports say it is disliked as imitation of non-Muslims, but the relied-upon position is that it is not disliked. (2) Wearing a sword or similar weapon is not disliked if the movement does not distract; if it does distract, it is disliked unless needed. (3) Not inserting the hands into the farji (a type of cloak) or shiqq (a garment slit) is not disliked on the chosen opinion. (4) Facing a mushaf (Quran) or a hanging sword is not disliked because these are not objects of worship; facing a Quran is not imitation of the People of the Book (who would pray towards scripture), while a sword is a weapon and the Quran even commands taking weapons in prayer context. (5) Facing the back of a seated person talking is not disliked, as per practice of Ibn Umar. (6) Facing a candle or lamp is not disliked because it does not resemble worship of fire-worshippers. (7) Prostrating on a carpet with images (of animate beings) is not disliked if one does not prostrate directly on the images themselves, as per al-Jami' al-Saghir, because it shows contempt for the images by stepping on them. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah from the core six books and attested in later compilations.

Key Terms
الوسط (al-wasaṭ): The waist or middle of the body, specifically binding or tightening the garment at the waist.
الفرجي (al-farajī): A type of outer garment or cloak with a slit (shiq) for the hands, common in classical Arab dress.
الشق (al-shiqq): Slit or opening in a garment, especially the farji garment.
المصحف (al-mushaf): A physical copy of the Quran.
التقليد (al-taqallud): Wearing a sword or similar weapon suspended from the shoulder or belt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it not disliked to face a hanging sword during prayer according to this passage?
A) Because the sword is a beautiful object
B) Because the Quran commands taking weapons, and it facilitates readiness
C) Because it is an imitation of the Magians
D) Because it helps in focusing on prayer

Key Takeaway
A wide range of practical actions are permissible in prayer as long as they do not cause distraction or imitate non-Muslim worship.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
Tying the Waist and Wearing a Sword in Prayer
Rulings on tying waist and wearing a sword with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tying the waist and wearing a sword during prayer, and identify the condition that makes wearing a sword disliked.

Core Idea
Actions that aid preparation without distraction are not disliked, even if they involve extra movement.

The Prophet ﷺ encouraged preparedness in prayer. Tying one's waist and wearing a sword are permissible, but distraction nullifies the leniency. This lesson clarifies the rulings and proofs for these two common actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
Tying the waist (shadd al-wasat) and wearing a sword (taqallud bi-sayf) are ruled 'not disliked' (la yukrah).
The default is permissibility unless a specific prohibition is proven.
2
Analyze the condition for the sword
The ruling depends on whether the sword distracts the worshipper. If it does not occupy his mind, it is not disliked; if it distracts, it becomes makruh unless he needs to carry it.
Distraction is the key factor, not the act itself.
3
Examine the minority opinion on tying waist
A minority view (from al-Ghiyathiyya) deems it disliked as imitation of the People of the Book. The Hanafi response: intention matters—tying aids worship, so it is not imitation.
The majority of Hanafi authorities prefer the view that it is not disliked.
4
Apply to modern scenarios
Wearing a belt or a watch does not distract and can be analogized to tying the waist. Carrying a necessary weapon (e.g., security guard) is similar to wearing a sword.
The principle is: any action that does not occupy the mind and aids readiness is permissible.
