Chapter on what is not disliked for the praying person from actions. It is not disliked for him to tie his waist. Nor to wear a sword or similar, if he is not occupied by its movement. Nor not inserting his hands into the slits of his garment and its side opening, according to the chosen view. Nor facing a mushaf, or a hanging sword, or the back of a seated person talking. Or a candle, or a lamp, according to the sound. And prostrating on a mat with images, if he does not prostrate on them. Commentary: (It is not disliked for him to tie his waist because it does not occupy the mind, as in al-Burhan; and it involves preparing for worship of his Lord, so it is not disliked, as in al-Bazzaziyya. In Sharh al-Munya from al-Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani that he used to say: if he prays with a cloak (qaba') and his waist is not tied, then he is doing poorly. Similarly in al-Khulasa, and in al-Bahr from al-Ghiyathiyya: it is disliked because it is the practice of the People of the Book. (Nor) is it disliked (for the praying person to wear a sword or similar if he is not occupied by its movement); if it occupies him, it is disliked if he does not need to carry it, as in al-Burhan. (Nor) is it disliked (not inserting his hands into the slits of his garment and its side opening, according to the chosen view), similarly in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya, because it does not occupy the mind. (Nor) is it disliked (facing a mushaf, or a hanging sword, because they are not worshipped; some people disliked that, we say: as for the mushaf, the People of the Book do it for reading from it, and it is disliked for us, even invalidating as we have mentioned, but our discussion is about merely it being in front of the worshipper, so it is not imitating them. As for the sword, Allah said: 'Let them take their weapons' [Quran 4:102]; if the sword is hung before him, it is easier for him to take it when needed, so it does not necessitate dislike. And the staff (anaza) was planted before the Prophet ﷺ, and he prayed towards it, and it is a weapon as we have mentioned.) (Or the back of a seated person talking according to the chosen view, because of the saying of Nafi': Ibn 'Umar, when he could not find a pillar, would say to me: turn your back to me.) (Or a candle or a lamp according to the sound view, because it does not resemble worship, since the Magians do not worship such things, but only if the fire is blazing, as in Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Tajnis, and al-Burhan. In al-Bahr, Ibn Qutayba said in Adab al-Katib in the chapter on words with two pronunciations where people use the weaker one: al-sham' (candle) with sukun, but the proper is with fatha on the mim.) (Nor) is it disliked (prostration on a mat with images) of living things (if one does not prostrate on them), and this is the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir, because it is a degradation of them, since they are trampled under feet, so it is not disliked, as when a cushion is thrown down, contrary to when the cushion is set up or the image is on a curtain, because that is veneration of them. And it was said: praying on something with an image is disliked even if one does not prostrate on the image, based on what was stated in the original text (al-Asl), because what one prays on is honored relative to other mats, so it involves veneration of the image, and we have been commanded to degrade images, so it is disliked. (And) it is not disliked (killing a snake) of all types according to the sound view, whether it is a jinn-snake (white) or non-jinn (black). This is regarding the prayer. As for fearing harm from jinn, it is better to refrain from what has a sign of jinn, because if it shows itself, it has violated the covenant of the Prophet ﷺ with the jinn that they should not enter the houses of his ummah nor show themselves; the violator is a traitor, so harm is feared from him or from his people. And in al-Muhit, they said: it is better not to kill the white snake that walks straight, because it is a jinn; the Prophet said: 'Kill the one with two stripes and the one with a stumpy tail, and beware of the white snake, for it is from the jinn.' If one sees a snake outside prayer and suspects it is a jinn, he should say to it: 'Leave the way of the Muslims and fear Allah and go'; if it passes, fine, otherwise leave it. Al-Tahawi said: there is no harm in killing all because of the covenant we have reported. And it was said: warn it, and if it refuses, kill it. These are three opinions; the best is to refrain due to fear of harm, because if it refuses to pass, it intends harm, so one leaves it to avoid it. (And) killing (a scorpion, if the praying person fears harm from both) i.e., the snake and scorpion, (even if with multiple blows and turning away from the qibla, according to the most apparent view). We restricted it to fear of harm because in al-Bahr from al-Nihaya from al-Jami' al-Saghir al-Burhani: 'They are permitted to be killed in prayer only if they pass in front of him and he fears they will harm him; otherwise it is disliked.' And in al-Bazzaziyya: 'Killing a snake with one or multiple strokes, if he fears its harm, does not invalidate and is not disliked according to the most apparent view; if safe, it is disliked.' Because of his saying: 'Kill the two black ones in prayer: the snake and the scorpion' reported by the four Sunan; al-Tirmidhi said it is a sound hadith, and its generality includes the need for much action. And it was said: it invalidates with numerous blows, like treating a passerby when he does much, although...
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Nur al-Idah, listing actions that are not disliked (makruh) during prayer. The commentator expands each ruling with proofs, citations, and occasional differences of opinion. The rulings covered are:

1. Tying the waist: Not disliked because it does not distract and helps the worshipper prepare for worship, though a minority opinion from al-Ghiyathiyya considers it disliked as imitation of Jews.

2. Wearing a sword or similar: Not disliked if it does not occupy the worshipper; if it occupies him and he has no need, it is disliked.

3. Not inserting hands into garment slits: Not disliked according to the chosen view.

4. Facing a mushaf or hanging sword: Not disliked because they are not objects of worship. Some scholars disliked it, but the Hanafi response distinguishes between using them as a sutra (which is fine) and imitating the People of the Book (which is not applicable here). The sword is supported by Quran 4:102 and the anaza (staff) used by the Prophet.

5. Facing the back of a seated person talking: Permissible based on the practice of Ibn 'Umar.

6. Facing a candle or lamp: Not disliked, contrary to possible resemblance to Magian fire-worship, because they are not blazing fires.

7. Prostrating on a mat with images of living things: Not disliked if one does not prostrate directly on the images, as per al-Jami' al-Saghir, because it degrades the images. However, if the image is on a curtain or a cushion set up respectfully, it is disliked due to veneration. There is a difference of opinion.

8. Killing a snake or scorpion during prayer: Not disliked if one fears harm, even with multiple blows or turning away from qibla. The hadith 'Kill the two black ones in prayer' supports this. There is a special ruling for white snakes (believed to be jinn): it is better not to kill because they may be from the jinn who have a covenant with the Prophet, but if they show themselves aggressively, they are considered violators. Three opinions are given: al-Tahawi permits killing all; others advise warning first; the preferred view is to leave due to potential harm.

The passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of deriving rulings from primary texts (Quran, Sunnah) and scholarly consensus, with attention to practical details.

Key Terms
الوسط (al-wasat): The waist; tying it refers to securing the garment with a belt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, when is wearing a sword in prayer disliked?
A) Always disliked
B) Disliked only if it occupies the worshipper and he does not need to carry it
C) Disliked only if the sword is drawn
D) Never disliked

Key Takeaway
Tying the waist and wearing a sword are permissible in prayer if they do not cause distraction, with the sword becoming disliked only when distracting and unnecessary.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Facing the Mushaf, Sword, or Seated Person in Prayer
Rulings on objects placed in front of the worshipper

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why facing a mushaf, hanging sword, or the back of a seated person is not disliked in Hanafi fiqh, and evaluate the counterargument based on imitation of non-Muslims.

Core Idea
Objects that are not worshipped or do not mimic other religions' rituals are valid as sutrah and do not make prayer disliked.

The direction one faces in prayer matters, but not all objects of respect or authority are problematic. This lesson explores the rulings on facing a mushaf, a hanging sword, or a seated person's back, addressing concerns of imitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify each object and the ruling
Facing a mushaf (open Qur'an), a hanging sword, or the back of a seated person who is talking are all ruled 'not disliked' (la yukrah).
The ruling applies to these specific conditions.
2
Analyze the proof for the sword
Qur'an 4:102 commands taking weapons, and the Prophet prayed towards an 'anaza (spear). Thus a hanging sword is a weapon, not an object of worship.
Proof from both Qur'an and Sunnah.
3
Examine the dispute on imitation
Some scholars argued that facing a mushaf or sword imitates Jews or Magians. The Hanafi response distinguishes between using them as a sutrah (permissible) and the act of reading from the mushaf or worshipping fire.
The key is intention and function.
4
Apply to the seated person
Facing the back of a seated person talking is based on Ibn 'Umar's practice. It prevents passing in front of the worshipper and is practical when no sutrah is available.
This is a dispensation for crowded mosques.

يكون تشبيهاً بهم، وأما السيف فقد قال تعالى: ﴿وَلْيَأْخُذُوا أَسْلِحَتَهُمْ [النساء : ١٠٢]، وإذا كان السيف معلقاً بين يديه كان أمكن لأخذه إذا احتاج إليه، فلا يوجـب الكـراهـة، » وَقَدْ كَانَتِ وهـي البيضاء، أو غير جنية وهي السوداء، هذا بالنظر لأمر الصَّلاة، وأما بالنظر لخشية الأذى مـن الجـن، فالأولى إمساك عما فيه علامة ،الجن، لأنها إذا أظهرت نفسها، فقد نقضت عهد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الذي عاهد به الجان، أن لا يدخلوا بيوت أمته، ولا يظهروا أنفسهم، وناقض العهد خائن، فيخشى منه، أو ممـن من أهله الضرر . رر بقتله في ( المحيط» قالوا: ينبغي أن لا تقتل الحية البيضاء التي تمشي مستوية؛ لأنها جان اقْتُلُوا الأسْوَدَين في ن في الصَّلاةِ، الحَيَّةَ والعَقْرَبَ ) رواه أصحاب السنن الأربعة، قال الترمذي حديث صحيح، وهو بإطلاقه يشمل المحتاج إلى العمل الكثير ، وقيل : تفسد بما يكثر من الضرب، كعلاج المار إذا أكثر مـع أنـه
Chapter on what is not disliked for the praying person from actions. It is not disliked for him to tie his waist. Nor to wear a sword or similar, if he is not occupied by its movement. Nor not inserting his hands into the slits of his garment and its side opening, according to the chosen view. Nor facing a mushaf, or a hanging sword, or the back of a seated person talking. Or a candle, or a lamp, according to the sound. And prostrating on a mat with images, if he does not prostrate on them. Commentary: (It is not disliked for him to tie his waist because it does not occupy the mind, as in al-Burhan; and it involves preparing for worship of his Lord, so it is not disliked, as in al-Bazzaziyya. In Sharh al-Munya from al-Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani that he used to say: if he prays with a cloak (qaba') and his waist is not tied, then he is doing poorly. Similarly in al-Khulasa, and in al-Bahr from al-Ghiyathiyya: it is disliked because it is the practice of the People of the Book. (Nor) is it disliked (for the praying person to wear a sword or similar if he is not occupied by its movement); if it occupies him, it is disliked if he does not need to carry it, as in al-Burhan. (Nor) is it disliked (not inserting his hands into the slits of his garment and its side opening, according to the chosen view), similarly in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya, because it does not occupy the mind. (Nor) is it disliked (facing a mushaf, or a hanging sword, because they are not worshipped; some people disliked that, we say: as for the mushaf, the People of the Book do it for reading from it, and it is disliked for us, even invalidating as we have mentioned, but our discussion is about merely it being in front of the worshipper, so it is not imitating them. As for the sword, Allah said: 'Let them take their weapons' [Quran 4:102]; if the sword is hung before him, it is easier for him to take it when needed, so it does not necessitate dislike. And the staff (anaza) was planted before the Prophet ﷺ, and he prayed towards it, and it is a weapon as we have mentioned.) (Or the back of a seated person talking according to the chosen view, because of the saying of Nafi': Ibn 'Umar, when he could not find a pillar, would say to me: turn your back to me.) (Or a candle or a lamp according to the sound view, because it does not resemble worship, since the Magians do not worship such things, but only if the fire is blazing, as in Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Tajnis, and al-Burhan. In al-Bahr, Ibn Qutayba said in Adab al-Katib in the chapter on words with two pronunciations where people use the weaker one: al-sham' (candle) with sukun, but the proper is with fatha on the mim.) (Nor) is it disliked (prostration on a mat with images) of living things (if one does not prostrate on them), and this is the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir, because it is a degradation of them, since they are trampled under feet, so it is not disliked, as when a cushion is thrown down, contrary to when the cushion is set up or the image is on a curtain, because that is veneration of them. And it was said: praying on something with an image is disliked even if one does not prostrate on the image, based on what was stated in the original text (al-Asl), because what one prays on is honored relative to other mats, so it involves veneration of the image, and we have been commanded to degrade images, so it is disliked. (And) it is not disliked (killing a snake) of all types according to the sound view, whether it is a jinn-snake (white) or non-jinn (black). This is regarding the prayer. As for fearing harm from jinn, it is better to refrain from what has a sign of jinn, because if it shows itself, it has violated the covenant of the Prophet ﷺ with the jinn that they should not enter the houses of his ummah nor show themselves; the violator is a traitor, so harm is feared from him or from his people. And in al-Muhit, they said: it is better not to kill the white snake that walks straight, because it is a jinn; the Prophet said: 'Kill the one with two stripes and the one with a stumpy tail, and beware of the white snake, for it is from the jinn.' If one sees a snake outside prayer and suspects it is a jinn, he should say to it: 'Leave the way of the Muslims and fear Allah and go'; if it passes, fine, otherwise leave it. Al-Tahawi said: there is no harm in killing all because of the covenant we have reported. And it was said: warn it, and if it refuses, kill it. These are three opinions; the best is to refrain due to fear of harm, because if it refuses to pass, it intends harm, so one leaves it to avoid it. (And) killing (a scorpion, if the praying person fears harm from both) i.e., the snake and scorpion, (even if with multiple blows and turning away from the qibla, according to the most apparent view). We restricted it to fear of harm because in al-Bahr from al-Nihaya from al-Jami' al-Saghir al-Burhani: 'They are permitted to be killed in prayer only if they pass in front of him and he fears they will harm him; otherwise it is disliked.' And in al-Bazzaziyya: 'Killing a snake with one or multiple strokes, if he fears its harm, does not invalidate and is not disliked according to the most apparent view; if safe, it is disliked.' Because of his saying: 'Kill the two black ones in prayer: the snake and the scorpion' reported by the four Sunan; al-Tirmidhi said it is a sound hadith, and its generality includes the need for much action. And it was said: it invalidates with numerous blows, like treating a passerby when he does much, although...
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Nur al-Idah, listing actions that are not disliked (makruh) during prayer. The commentator expands each ruling with proofs, citations, and occasional differences of opinion. The rulings covered are:

1. Tying the waist: Not disliked because it does not distract and helps the worshipper prepare for worship, though a minority opinion from al-Ghiyathiyya considers it disliked as imitation of Jews.

2. Wearing a sword or similar: Not disliked if it does not occupy the worshipper; if it occupies him and he has no need, it is disliked.

3. Not inserting hands into garment slits: Not disliked according to the chosen view.

4. Facing a mushaf or hanging sword: Not disliked because they are not objects of worship. Some scholars disliked it, but the Hanafi response distinguishes between using them as a sutra (which is fine) and imitating the People of the Book (which is not applicable here). The sword is supported by Quran 4:102 and the anaza (staff) used by the Prophet.

5. Facing the back of a seated person talking: Permissible based on the practice of Ibn 'Umar.

6. Facing a candle or lamp: Not disliked, contrary to possible resemblance to Magian fire-worship, because they are not blazing fires.

7. Prostrating on a mat with images of living things: Not disliked if one does not prostrate directly on the images, as per al-Jami' al-Saghir, because it degrades the images. However, if the image is on a curtain or a cushion set up respectfully, it is disliked due to veneration. There is a difference of opinion.

8. Killing a snake or scorpion during prayer: Not disliked if one fears harm, even with multiple blows or turning away from qibla. The hadith 'Kill the two black ones in prayer' supports this. Key Terms
العَنْزَة (al-'anazah): A short spear staff used by the Prophet as a sutrah.

According to the passage, why is facing a hanging sword not disliked?
A) Because swords are not worshipped
B) Because the Prophet prayed towards an 'anaza
C) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
Facing a mushaf, hanging sword, or back of a seated person is not disliked; the key is that these are not objects of worship and do not involve imitative acts of non-Muslims.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Prostration on a Mat with Images
Ruling on prostrating on a mat with images

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on prostrating on a mat with images of living beings and identify the conditions that affect the ruling.

Core Idea
If the image is not prostrated upon and is degraded by being stepped on, it is not disliked; veneration of images makes it disliked.

Images of living beings are highly regulated in Islam. During prayer, the placement of such images on the ground can affect the ruling. This lesson clarifies when prostrating on a mat with images is permissible and when it becomes disliked.

Guided Path
1
State the basic ruling
Prostrating on a mat (bisaat) containing images of living beings is not disliked if the worshipper does not prostrate directly on the images.
This is the narration from al-Jami' al-Saghir.
2
Understand the reasoning
The images are degraded because they are trodden underfoot, so there is no veneration (i'zaz). In fact, it is a form of humiliation (ihanah), which is commanded.
Degradation of images is praiseworthy.
3
Identify when it becomes disliked
If the image is on a cushion placed upright or on a curtain, it is disliked because that constitutes veneration. Similarly, if the mat is considered honored (e.g., fine carpet), some scholars say it is disliked.
The distinction is based on whether the image is treated with respect.
4
Analyze the difference of opinion
Some Hanafi scholars hold that praying on any surface with an image is disliked regardless of location, because the mat itself is honored relative to other mats.
The text presents both views but leans towards the view that it is not disliked if the image is on the ground.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

التَّوَجُهُ لمصحف، أو سيف معلّق لأنهما لا يعبدان، ومن الناس من كره ذلك، قلنا: أمـا المصحف فأهل الكتاب يفعلونه للقراءة منه، وهو مكروه عندنا بل مفسد على ما قدمناه، وكلامنا في مجرد كونه أمام المصلي، فلا يكون تشبيهاً بهم، وأما السيف فقد قال تعالى: ﴿وَلْيَأْخُذُوا أَسْلِحَتَهُمْ [النساء : ١٠٢]، وإذا كان السيف معلقاً بين يديه كان أمكن لأخذه إذا احتاج إليه، فلا يوجـب الكـراهـة، » وَقَدْ كَانَتِ العَنْزَةُ تركز بين يدي النبي ، فيُصَلِّي إليها، وهو سلاح كما قدمناه )، (أو ظهر قاعد يتحدث في المختار، لقول نافع: «كَانَ ابْنَ عُمَر إذا لَمْ يَجِدْ سَبِيلاً إلى سَارِيَةٍ قَالَ لِي: ول بِظَهْرِكَ » )، (أو شمع. أو سراج على الصحيح؛ لأنه لا يشبه التعبد؛ لأن المجوس لا يعبدون مثل هذا، بل إذا كانت النار مضرمة ، كما في غاية البيان » و « التجنيس » و « البرهان»، وفي « البحر ) قال ابن قتيبة في أدب الكاتب في باب ما جاء فيه لغتان استعمل الناس أضعفهما: الشمع بالسكون، والأوجه فتح الميم، (ولا) يكره ( السجود على بساط فيه تصاوير) ذي روح (لم يَسْجُدْ عليها)، وهذه رواية ( الجامع الصغير ) لأنه استهانة لها، لأنها تداس وتوطأ بالأرجل فلا يكره، كما إذا كانت الوسادة ملقاة، بخلاف ما إذا كانت الوسادة منصوبة، أو كانت الصورة على الستر؛ لأنـه تعظيم لها، وقيل: تكره الصلاة على ما فيه صورة، وإن لم يقع السجود عليها، بناء على ما أطلقه في ه في الأصل؛ لأن ما يصلي عليه معظم بالنسبة إلى سائر البسط، فكان فيه تعظيـم الصـورة. وقد امرنا بإهانتها ) فتكره، (وَ) لا يكره (قَتْلُ حيةٍ) بجميع أنواعها في الصحيح، سواء كانت جنيـة وهـي البيضاء، أو غير جنية وهي السوداء، هذا بالنظر لأمر الصَّلاة، وأما بالنظر لخشية الأذى مـن الجـن، فالأولى إمساك عما فيه علامة ،الجن، لأنها إذا أظهرت نفسها، فقد نقضت عهد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الذي عاهد به الجان، أن لا يدخلوا بيوت أمته، ولا يظهروا أنفسهم، وناقض العهد خائن، فيخشى منه، أو ممـن من أهله الضرر . رر بقتله في ( المحيط» قالوا: ينبغي أن لا تقتل الحية البيضاء التي تمشي مستوية؛ لأنها جان لقوله : « اقتلوا ذات الطفيتين، والأبتر، وإياكم والحية البيضاء، فإنَّهَا مِنَ الجن» انتهى. وإذا رأى حية خارج الصلاة وشك أنه جني يقول له: خل طريق المسلمين واتق الله ومر، فإن مرَّ فيها، وإلا تركه. وقال الطحاوي: لا بأس بقتل الكل للعهد الـذي رويناه انتهى، وقيل: ينذرها فإن أبت قتلها. فهذه ثلاثة أقوال والأولى الترك خشية الضرر؛ لأنها إذا أبـت المـرور قصدت الأذى، فتترك تحاشياً عن عنه، (وَ) لا قتل (عقرب، خاف) المصلي (أذاهما) أي: الحيـة والعـقـرب، ولَوْ) قتلهما (بِضَرْبَاتٍ، وانحراف عن القبلة، في الأظهر ) قيدنـا بـخـوف الأذى لمـا قـال في البحر » ، عن « النهاية » ، عن ( الجامع الصغير البرهاني : إنما يباح قتلهما في الصلاة إذا مرت بين يديه وخاف أن تؤذيه، وإلا فيكره انتهى ولما قال في ( البزازية » : قتل الحية بضربة أو ضربــات لـو خشي أذاها لا تفسد، ولا يكره في الأظهر، ومع الأمن يكره انتهى، لقوله : ( اقْتُلُوا الأسْوَدَين في ن في الصَّلاةِ، الحَيَّةَ والعَقْرَبَ ) رواه أصحاب السنن الأربعة، قال الترمذي حديث صحيح، وهو بإطلاقه يشمل المحتاج إلى العمل الكثير ، وقيل : تفسد بما يكثر من الضرب، كعلاج المار إذا أكثر مـع أنـه
Chapter on what is not disliked for the praying person from actions. It is not disliked for him to tie his waist. Nor to wear a sword or similar, if he is not occupied by its movement. Nor not inserting his hands into the slits of his garment and its side opening, according to the chosen view. Nor facing a mushaf, or a hanging sword, or the back of a seated person talking. Or a candle, or a lamp, according to the sound. And prostrating on a mat with images, if he does not prostrate on them. Commentary: (It is not disliked for him to tie his waist because it does not occupy the mind, as in al-Burhan; and it involves preparing for worship of his Lord, so it is not disliked, as in al-Bazzaziyya. In Sharh al-Munya from al-Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani that he used to say: if he prays with a cloak (qaba') and his waist is not tied, then he is doing poorly. Similarly in al-Khulasa, and in al-Bahr from al-Ghiyathiyya: it is disliked because it is the practice of the People of the Book. (Nor) is it disliked (for the praying person to wear a sword or similar if he is not occupied by its movement); if it occupies him, it is disliked if he does not need to carry it, as in al-Burhan. (Nor) is it disliked (not inserting his hands into the slits of his garment and its side opening, according to the chosen view), similarly in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya, because it does not occupy the mind. (Nor) is it disliked (facing a mushaf, or a hanging sword, because they are not worshipped; some people disliked that, we say: as for the mushaf, the People of the Book do it for reading from it, and it is disliked for us, even invalidating as we have mentioned, but our discussion is about merely it being in front of the worshipper, so it is not imitating them. As for the sword, Allah said: 'Let them take their weapons' [Quran 4:102]; if the sword is hung before him, it is easier for him to take it when needed, so it does not necessitate dislike. And the staff (anaza) was planted before the Prophet ﷺ, and he prayed towards it, and it is a weapon as we have mentioned.) (Or the back of a seated person talking according to the chosen view, because of the saying of Nafi': Ibn 'Umar, when he could not find a pillar, would say to me: turn your back to me.) (Or a candle or a lamp according to the sound view, because it does not resemble worship, since the Magians do not worship such things, but only if the fire is blazing, as in Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Tajnis, and al-Burhan. In al-Bahr, Ibn Qutayba said in Adab al-Katib in the chapter on words with two pronunciations where people use the weaker one: al-sham' (candle) with sukun, but the proper is with fatha on the mim.) (Nor) is it disliked (prostration on a mat with images) of living things (if one does not prostrate on them), and this is the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir, because it is a degradation of them, since they are trampled under feet, so it is not disliked, as when a cushion is thrown down, contrary to when the cushion is set up or the image is on a curtain, because that is veneration of them. And it was said: praying on something with an image is disliked even if one does not prostrate on the image, based on what was stated in the original text (al-Asl), because what one prays on is honored relative to other mats, so it involves veneration of the image, and we have been commanded to degrade images, so it is disliked. (And) it is not disliked (killing a snake) of all types according to the sound view, whether it is a jinn-snake (white) or non-jinn (black). This is regarding the prayer. As for fearing harm from jinn, it is better to refrain from what has a sign of jinn, because if it shows itself, it has violated the covenant of the Prophet ﷺ with the jinn that they should not enter the houses of his ummah nor show themselves; the violator is a traitor, so harm is feared from him or from his people. And in al-Muhit, they said: it is better not to kill the white snake that walks straight, because it is a jinn; the Prophet said: 'Kill the one with two stripes and the one with a stumpy tail, and beware of the white snake, for it is from the jinn.' If one sees a snake outside prayer and suspects it is a jinn, he should say to it: 'Leave the way of the Muslims and fear Allah and go'; if it passes, fine, otherwise leave it. Al-Tahawi said: there is no harm in killing all because of the covenant we have reported. And it was said: warn it, and if it refuses, kill it. These are three opinions; the best is to refrain due to fear of harm, because if it refuses to pass, it intends harm, so one leaves it to avoid it. (And) killing (a scorpion, if the praying person fears harm from both) i.e., the snake and scorpion, (even if with multiple blows and turning away from the qibla, according to the most apparent view). We restricted it to fear of harm because in al-Bahr from al-Nihaya from al-Jami' al-Saghir al-Burhani: 'They are permitted to be killed in prayer only if they pass in front of him and he fears they will harm him; otherwise it is disliked.' And in al-Bazzaziyya: 'Killing a snake with one or multiple strokes, if he fears its harm, does not invalidate and is not disliked according to the most apparent view; if safe, it is disliked.' Because of his saying: 'Kill the two black ones in prayer: the snake and the scorpion' reported by the four Sunan; al-Tirmidhi said it is a sound hadith, and its generality includes the need for much action. And it was said: it invalidates with numerous blows, like treating a passerby when he does much, although...
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Nur al-Idah, listing actions that are not disliked (makruh) during prayer. The commentator expands each ruling with proofs, citations, and occasional differences of opinion. The rulings covered are:

1. Tying the waist: Not disliked because it does not distract and helps the worshipper prepare for worship, though a minority opinion from al-Ghiyathiyya considers it disliked as imitation of Jews.

2. Wearing a sword or similar: Not disliked if it does not occupy the worshipper; if it occupies him and he has no need, it is disliked.

3. Not inserting hands into garment slits: Not disliked according to the chosen view.

4. Facing a mushaf or hanging sword: Not disliked because they are not objects of worship. Some scholars disliked it, but the Hanafi response distinguishes between using them as a sutra (which is fine) and imitating the People of the Book (which is not applicable here). The sword is supported by Quran 4:102 and the anaza (staff) used by the Prophet.

5. Facing the back of a seated person talking: Permissible based on the practice of Ibn 'Umar.

6. Facing a candle or lamp: Not disliked, contrary to possible resemblance to Magian fire-worship, because they are not blazing fires.

7. Prostrating on a mat with images of living things: Not disliked if one does not prostrate directly on the images, as per al-Jami' al-Saghir, because it degrades the images. However, if the image is on a curtain or a cushion set up respectfully, it is disliked due to veneration. There is a difference of opinion.

8. Killing a snake or scorpion during prayer: Not disliked if one fears harm, even with multiple blows or turning away from qibla. The hadith 'Kill the two black ones in prayer' supports this. There is a special ruling for white snakes (believed to be jinn): it is better not to kill because they may be from the jinn who have a covenant with the Prophet, but if they show themselves aggressively, they are considered violators. Three opinions are given: al-Tahawi permits killing all; others advise warning first; the preferred view is to leave due to potential harm.

The passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of deriving rulings from primary texts (Quran, Sunnah) and scholarly consensus, with attention to practical details.

Key Terms
تصاوير (tasawir): Images, specifically of living beings (dhi ruh).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir, when is prostrating on a mat with images disliked?
A) Always disliked
B) Only if the worshipper prostrates directly on the images
C) Only if the image is on a curtain
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Prostration on images of living beings is not disliked as long as the image is degraded (trodden upon) and not directly prostrated on; veneration of the image makes it disliked.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Killing Snakes and Scorpions During Prayer
Ruling on killing snakes and scorpions in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing snakes and scorpions during prayer, identify conditions that affect permissibility, and distinguish between jinn-snakes and ordinary snakes.

Core Idea
Killing a dangerous snake or scorpion during prayer is permissible and not disliked if one fears harm, even with multiple blows or turning away.

The Prophet ﷺ explicitly permitted killing certain harmful creatures during prayer. This lesson details the ruling, the conditions, and the special consideration for white snakes believed to be jinn.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling
Killing a snake or scorpion during prayer is not disliked (la yukrah) if the worshipper fears harm from it.
This is based on the hadith 'Kill the two black ones in prayer: the snake and the scorpion'.
2
Identify the conditions
The permission requires fear of harm (khawf al-adha). If there is no fear, killing becomes disliked (makruh). Even if many blows are needed or one turns away from the qibla, it does not invalidate the prayer according to the most apparent view.
The act of killing may involve extra movements, but it is excused due to necessity.
3
Understand the white snake exception
A white snake that walks straight is believed to be a jinn that has a covenant with the Prophet. Killing it is discouraged (first to avoid) because it may be a jinn that violated the covenant only by appearing. The preferred view is to warn it first.
Three opinions are presented: kill all (al-Tahawi), warn then kill, or avoid entirely. The preferred view is to leave it due to fear of retaliation.
4
Apply to scorpion and other pests
The same ruling applies to scorpions. Other harmful animals (like centipedes) may be analogized if they pose similar danger.
The hadith is specific to these two, but qiyas extends the ruling.

إذا أكثر مـع أنـه
Chapter on what is not disliked for the praying person from actions. It is not disliked for him to tie his waist. Nor to wear a sword or similar, if he is not occupied by its movement. Nor not inserting his hands into the slits of his garment and its side opening, according to the chosen view. Nor facing a mushaf, or a hanging sword, or the back of a seated person talking. Or a candle, or a lamp, according to the sound. And prostrating on a mat with images, if he does not prostrate on them. Commentary: (It is not disliked for him to tie his waist because it does not occupy the mind, as in al-Burhan; and it involves preparing for worship of his Lord, so it is not disliked, as in al-Bazzaziyya. In Sharh al-Munya from al-Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani that he used to say: if he prays with a cloak (qaba') and his waist is not tied, then he is doing poorly. Similarly in al-Khulasa, and in al-Bahr from al-Ghiyathiyya: it is disliked because it is the practice of the People of the Book. (Nor) is it disliked (for the praying person to wear a sword or similar if he is not occupied by its movement); if it occupies him, it is disliked if he does not need to carry it, as in al-Burhan. (Nor) is it disliked (not inserting his hands into the slits of his garment and its side opening, according to the chosen view), similarly in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya, because it does not occupy the mind. (Nor) is it disliked (facing a mushaf, or a hanging sword, because they are not worshipped; some people disliked that, we say: as for the mushaf, the People of the Book do it for reading from it, and it is disliked for us, even invalidating as we have mentioned, but our discussion is about merely it being in front of the worshipper, so it is not imitating them. As for the sword, Allah said: 'Let them take their weapons' [Quran 4:102]; if the sword is hung before him, it is easier for him to take it when needed, so it does not necessitate dislike. And the staff (anaza) was planted before the Prophet ﷺ, and he prayed towards it, and it is a weapon as we have mentioned.) (Or the back of a seated person talking according to the chosen view, because of the saying of Nafi': Ibn 'Umar, when he could not find a pillar, would say to me: turn your back to me.) (Or a candle or a lamp according to the sound view, because it does not resemble worship, since the Magians do not worship such things, but only if the fire is blazing, as in Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Tajnis, and al-Burhan. In al-Bahr, Ibn Qutayba said in Adab al-Katib in the chapter on words with two pronunciations where people use the weaker one: al-sham' (candle) with sukun, but the proper is with fatha on the mim.) (Nor) is it disliked (prostration on a mat with images) of living things (if one does not prostrate on them), and this is the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir, because it is a degradation of them, since they are trampled under feet, so it is not disliked, as when a cushion is thrown down, contrary to when the cushion is set up or the image is on a curtain, because that is veneration of them. And it was said: praying on something with an image is disliked even if one does not prostrate on the image, based on what was stated in the original text (al-Asl), because what one prays on is honored relative to other mats, so it involves veneration of the image, and we have been commanded to degrade images, so it is disliked. (And) it is not disliked (killing a snake) of all types according to the sound view, whether it is a jinn-snake (white) or non-jinn (black). This is regarding the prayer. As for fearing harm from jinn, it is better to refrain from what has a sign of jinn, because if it shows itself, it has violated the covenant of the Prophet ﷺ with the jinn that they should not enter the houses of his ummah nor show themselves; the violator is a traitor, so harm is feared from him or from his people. And in al-Muhit, they said: it is better not to kill the white snake that walks straight, because it is a jinn; the Prophet said: 'Kill the one with two stripes and the one with a stumpy tail, and beware of the white snake, for it is from the jinn.' If one sees a snake outside prayer and suspects it is a jinn, he should say to it: 'Leave the way of the Muslims and fear Allah and go'; if it passes, fine, otherwise leave it. Al-Tahawi said: there is no harm in killing all because of the covenant we have reported. And it was said: warn it, and if it refuses, kill it. These are three opinions; the best is to refrain due to fear of harm, because if it refuses to pass, it intends harm, so one leaves it to avoid it. (And) killing (a scorpion, if the praying person fears harm from both) i.e., the snake and scorpion, (even if with multiple blows and turning away from the qibla, according to the most apparent view). We restricted it to fear of harm because in al-Bahr from al-Nihaya from al-Jami' al-Saghir al-Burhani: 'They are permitted to be killed in prayer only if they pass in front of him and he fears they will harm him; otherwise it is disliked.' And in al-Bazzaziyya: 'Killing a snake with one or multiple strokes, if he fears its harm, does not invalidate and is not disliked according to the most apparent view; if safe, it is disliked.' Because of his saying: 'Kill the two black ones in prayer: the snake and the scorpion' reported by the four Sunan; al-Tirmidhi said it is a sound hadith, and its generality includes the need for much action. And it was said: it invalidates with numerous blows, like treating a passerby when he does much, although...
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Nur al-Idah, listing actions that are not disliked (makruh) during prayer. The commentator expands each ruling with proofs, citations, and occasional differences of opinion. The rulings covered are:

1. Tying the waist: Not disliked because it does not distract and helps the worshipper prepare for worship, though a minority opinion from al-Ghiyathiyya considers it disliked as imitation of Jews.

2. Wearing a sword or similar: Not disliked if it does not occupy the worshipper; if it occupies him and he has no need, it is disliked.

3. Not inserting hands into garment slits: Not disliked according to the chosen view.

4. Facing a mushaf or hanging sword: Not disliked because they are not objects of worship. Some scholars disliked it, but the Hanafi response distinguishes between using them as a sutra (which is fine) and imitating the People of the Book (which is not applicable here). The sword is supported by Quran 4:102 and the anaza (staff) used by the Prophet.

5. Facing the back of a seated person talking: Permissible based on the practice of Ibn 'Umar.

6. Facing a candle or lamp: Not disliked, contrary to possible resemblance to Magian fire-worship, because they are not blazing fires.

7. Prostrating on a mat with images of living things: Not disliked if one does not prostrate directly on the images, as per al-Jami' al-Saghir, because it degrades the images. However, if the image is on a curtain or a cushion set up respectfully, it is disliked due to veneration. There is a difference of opinion.

8. Killing a snake or scorpion during prayer: Not disliked if one fears harm, even with multiple blows or turning away from qibla. The hadith 'Kill the two black ones in prayer' supports this. There is a special ruling for white snakes (believed to be jinn): it is better not to kill because they may be from the jinn who have a covenant with the Prophet, but if they show themselves aggressively, they are considered violators. Three opinions are given: al-Tahawi permits killing all; others advise warning first; the preferred view is to leave due to potential harm.

The passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of deriving rulings from primary texts (Quran, Sunnah) and scholarly consensus, with attention to practical details.

Key Terms
الحية البيضاء (al-hayyat al-bayda'): White snake believed to be a jinn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on killing a white snake during prayer?
A) It is haram
B) It is permitted and recommended
C) It is better to avoid killing it despite permissibility
D) It invalidates the prayer

Key Takeaway
Killing snakes and scorpions during prayer is permissible when harm is feared, and does not invalidate the prayer even with multiple actions; however, white snakes (likely jinn) should be avoided if possible.

Killing Snakes and Scorpions in Prayer: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on killing harmful creatures in prayer with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on killing snakes and scorpions in prayer and explain the dalil from the hadith.

Core Idea
Killing a snake or scorpion in prayer is permissible only when fearing harm; without fear, it is disliked.

The source passage addresses a common scenario: what if a snake or scorpion appears during prayer? The Hanafi school provides clear guidance based on the Prophet's command and the principle of avoiding greater harm. This lesson unpacks the primary ruling and its textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine exactly what is being ruled upon: killing a snake or scorpion during prayer. The ruling is mubah (permissible) if one fears harm, otherwise makruh (disliked).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith 'Kill the two black ones in prayer: the snake and the scorpion.' This is a sahih hadith narrated by the four sunan compilers.
Sunan Abi Dawud (921), Ibn Majah (1245)
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'uqtulu' (kill) indicates a command. In Hanafi usul, a command generally indicates obligation. However, the context of prayer and the fear of harm make the command permissive (ibaha) rather than obligatory, as the act is otherwise disliked.
The hadith's generality includes both fear and safety; the condition of fear is derived from other texts and qiyas.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars argue that multiple strikes invalidate prayer. The Hanafi response: the harm from the sting can cause death, so it is analogous to walking after an impurity or drawing water from a well out of necessity, allowing many actions.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is that killing is permissible with fear, even with many strikes and turning away from qibla. Without fear, it is disliked but still valid.
Al-Bazzaziyya and al-Bahr affirm this.

به، قلنا : في هذا أمر آخر، وهو الضرر المؤدي لتلف النفس بلسعها، وصار كالمشي بعد سبق الحدث، والاستقاء من البئر انتهى. وفي السبعيات لأبي الليث: سبعة أشياء إذا رآها المصلي لا بأس بقتلها: الحية، والعقرب، والوزغة، والزنبور، والقراد، والبرغوث، والقمل. كذا في «مجمع الروايات» انتهى قلت وعلى هذا يزاد الفسفس والبعوض، والنمل المؤذي بالعض، ونحوها انتهى. وقدمنا ) أن أخذ القملة وقتلها مكروه في الصلاة عند الإمام، وقال: دفنها فيها أحب من قتلها، وقال محمد: بخلافه، وقال أبو يوسف بكراهتها، وقال صاحب البحر » : لعل الإمام إنما اختار دفـــن القملة؛ لما فيه من النزاهة عن إصابة دمها ليد القاتل، أو ثوبه في هذه الحالة، وإن كان معفواً عنـه انتهى. قلت: وبه صرح في شرح المنية » : دفنها أحب إن تيسر؛ لأن [ في ] قتلها إيجاد نجاسة على قول الشافعي؛ لأن قشرها نجس، وما دامت حية فهي طاهرة، ففي عدم قتلها تحرز عن الخلاف؛ لئلا يحمل النجاسة المانعة على قول بعض الأئمة، أو يلقيها في المسجد فكان أحب، ويحمل الإساءة، والكراهة المروية عن أبي حنيفة، وأبي يوسف على أخذها قصداً من غير عذر انتهى.
And killing a snake and scorpion, if he fears their harm; even with multiple strikes, and turning away from the qibla in the apparent view. It is like that as a veneration of it, and it is said: prayer on something with an image is disliked, even if prostration does not occur on it, based on what he stated in the original; because what one prays on is honored relative to other spreads, so there is veneration of the image. And we have been commanded to disgrace them, so it is disliked. And it is not disliked to kill a snake of all types in the correct view, whether it is a jinniyya (white) or non-jinniyya (black), this concerning the matter of prayer. As for concerning fear of harm from the jinn, it is better to refrain from what has a sign of the jinn, because if it shows itself, it has broken the covenant of the Prophet ﷺ that he made with the jinn, that they should not enter the houses of his ummah nor show themselves, and the covenant-breaker is treacherous, so harm is feared from it or from its people. It was repeated regarding killing it in al-Muhit: they said: the white snake that walks straight should not be killed, because it is a jinn, due to his saying: "Kill the one with two streaks and the one with a short tail, and beware of the white snake, for it is from the jinn." End. And if he sees a snake outside prayer and doubts whether it is a jinn, he says to it: clear the path of the Muslims and fear Allah and move on; if it moves on, fine, otherwise he leaves it. And al-Tahawi said: there is no harm in killing all due to the covenant we narrated. End. And it is said: he warns it; if it refuses, he kills it. These are three sayings, and the better view is to refrain out of fear of harm; because if it refuses to move on, it intends harm, so he leaves it to avoid it. And there is no killing of a scorpion, if the worshipper fears their harm, i.e., the snake and the scorpion, and even if he kills them with multiple strikes and turning away from the qibla in the apparent view. We restricted it to fear of harm because of what was said in al-Bahr from al-Nihaya from al-Jami' al-Saghir al-Burhani: it is only permissible to kill them in prayer if they pass between his hands and he fears they will harm him, otherwise it is disliked. End. And because of what was said in al-Bazzaziyya: killing a snake with one or multiple strikes, if he fears its harm, does not invalidate and is not disliked in the apparent view, and when safe it is disliked. End. Due to his saying: "Kill the two black ones in prayer: the snake and the scorpion" narrated by the authors of the four Sunan, al-Tirmidhi said it is a sahih hadith, and in its generality it includes the need for much action. And it is said: it invalidates if strikes are many, like treating a passerby if he does much, even though he is commanded to do it. We said: in this there is another matter: the harm leading to destruction of life by their sting, and it became like walking after a precedent hadath, and drawing water from a well. End. And in al-Sub'iyyat of Abu al-Layth: seven things which if the worshiper sees, there is no harm in killing them: the snake, the scorpion, the gecko, the wasp, the tick, the flea, and the louse. Similarly in Majma' al-Riwayat. End. I say: and on this are added the mosquito, the gnat, and harmful ants that bite, and the like. End. And we have stated that taking and killing a louse in prayer is disliked according to Imam, and he said: burying it in it is more beloved than killing it. And Muhammad said contrary to that, and Abu Yusuf said it is disliked. And the author of al-Bahr said: perhaps Imam only chose burying the louse because of the cleanliness from getting its blood on the hand or garment in this state, even if it is pardoned. End. I say: and it is stated explicitly in Sharh al-Munyah: burying it is more beloved if possible, because in killing it there is creating impurity according to the view of al-Shafi'i, because its shell is impure, and as long as it is alive it is pure, so by not killing it one avoids the disagreement, lest he carry the impure that prevents according to some imams, or throw it in the mosque, so it was more beloved. And the offensiveness and dislike narrated from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf are about taking it intentionally without excuse. End.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah discusses the ruling on killing snakes and scorpions during prayer. The author begins with the ruling: if a worshiper fears harm from a snake or scorpion, it is permissible to kill them even with multiple strikes and even if one turns away from the qibla. This is the apparent (zahir) position. The reasoning is that the command to kill these creatures in the hadith overrides the prohibition of extraneous actions in prayer. The hadith cited is the Prophet's ﷺ command: 'Kill the two black ones in prayer: the snake and the scorpion.' This is a sound hadith narrated by the four sunan compilers. The commentator then addresses a potential objection: that multiple strikes may invalidate the prayer, similar to treating a passerby with many actions. He refutes this by noting that the harm from the creature's sting can lead to death, which is a greater harm, analogous to walking after an impurity or drawing water from a well out of necessity. The passage then discusses the different types of snakes: the white snake (jinniyya) and the black snake (non-jinniyya). There is an intra-Hanafi difference: some scholars say the white snake should not be killed because it is a jinn that has a covenant with the Prophet ﷺ not to harm Muslims. The preferred view is to refrain from killing it out of fear of harm. The author also mentions the view of al-Tahawi who permits killing all snakes based on another covenant. The passage concludes with a list of seven creatures that may be killed in prayer without dislike, and adds others like mosquitoes and ants. There is also a discussion about killing lice: Imam Abu Hanifa prefers burying it over killing it to avoid impurity, while Imam Muhammad allows it and Imam Abu Yusuf dislikes it. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is to bury it if possible, to avoid the differing opinions of other imams.

Key Terms
حية (hayyah): Snake; includes both jinniyya (white) and non-jinniyya (black) types.
عقرب (aqrab): Scorpion; treated similarly to snakes in terms of permissibility of killing in prayer when fearing harm.
الأظهر (al-azhar): The apparent or more evident position within the Hanafi school, often the mufta bihi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the passage, what did the Prophet ﷺ command regarding snakes and scorpions in prayer?
A) To avoid killing them.
B) To kill them only if they attack.
C) To kill the two black ones.
D) To ignore them.

Key Takeaway
Killing a snake or scorpion in prayer is permissible when fearing harm, based on the Prophet's command and the principle of necessity; the prayer remains valid even with many actions.

The White Snake and Lice: Intra-Hanafi Nuances
Intra-Hanafi differences on white snake and lice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on killing the white snake in prayer and the preferred view on lice.

Core Idea
The white snake is a jinn with a covenant; better to leave it in prayer; for lice, burying is more beloved than killing.

While the general ruling on snakes is clear, the white snake (believed to be a jinn) presents special considerations. Similarly, lice are among the creatures that may be killed, but the Hanafi imams differ on whether to kill or bury them. This lesson explores these nuanced positions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on the white snake
The preferred view is to refrain from killing the white snake that walks straight, as it is a jinn with a covenant from the Prophet ﷺ not to harm Muslims.
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold this view.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam Muhammad and al-Tahawi permit killing all snakes, including the white one, arguing that the covenant is broken if it shows itself.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opposing side relies on the general command to kill snakes and scorpions, and argues that showing oneself constitutes breach of covenant.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is based on a specific hadith warning against the white snake, and caution due to the possibility of harm from the jinn. Out of precaution, one should warn it first and only kill if it attacks.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: In prayer, some Hanafis would kill a white snake that appears; others would leave it unless it attacks. The mufta bihi is to refrain.
Al-Muhit and al-Bahr prefer refraining.
6
Note the lice dispute
For lice, Abu Hanifa prefers burying them to avoid impurity (since dead lice may be impure per Shafi'i), while Muhammad permits killing and Abu Yusuf dislikes it. The relied-upon view is to bury if possible.
Sharh al-Munyah supports burying.

به، قلنا : في هذا أمر آخر، وهو الضرر المؤدي لتلف النفس بلسعها، وصار كالمشي بعد سبق الحدث، والاستقاء من البئر انتهى. وفي السبعيات لأبي الليث: سبعة أشياء إذا رآها المصلي لا بأس بقتلها: الحية، والعقرب، والوزغة، والزنبور، والقراد، والبرغوث، والقمل. كذا في «مجمع الروايات» انتهى قلت وعلى هذا يزاد الفسفس والبعوض، والنمل المؤذي بالعض، ونحوها انتهى. وقدمنا ) أن أخذ القملة وقتلها مكروه في الصلاة عند الإمام، وقال: دفنها فيها أحب من قتلها، وقال محمد: بخلافه، وقال أبو يوسف بكراهتها، وقال صاحب البحر » : لعل الإمام إنما اختار دفـــن القملة؛ لما فيه من النزاهة عن إصابة دمها ليد القاتل، أو ثوبه في هذه الحالة، وإن كان معفواً عنـه انتهى. قلت: وبه صرح في شرح المنية » : دفنها أحب إن تيسر؛ لأن [ في ] قتلها إيجاد نجاسة على قول الشافعي؛ لأن قشرها نجس، وما دامت حية فهي طاهرة، ففي عدم قتلها تحرز عن الخلاف؛ لئلا يحمل النجاسة المانعة على قول بعض الأئمة، أو يلقيها في المسجد فكان أحب، ويحمل الإساءة، والكراهة المروية عن أبي حنيفة، وأبي يوسف على أخذها قصداً من غير عذر انتهى.
And killing a snake and scorpion, if he fears their harm; even with multiple strikes, and turning away from the qibla in the apparent view. It is like that as a veneration of it, and it is said: prayer on something with an image is disliked, even if prostration does not occur on it, based on what he stated in the original; because what one prays on is honored relative to other spreads, so there is veneration of the image. And we have been commanded to disgrace them, so it is disliked. And it is not disliked to kill a snake of all types in the correct view, whether it is a jinniyya (white) or non-jinniyya (black), this concerning the matter of prayer. As for concerning fear of harm from the jinn, it is better to refrain from what has a sign of the jinn, because if it shows itself, it has broken the covenant of the Prophet ﷺ that he made with the jinn, that they should not enter the houses of his ummah nor show themselves, and the covenant-breaker is treacherous, so harm is feared from it or from its people. It was repeated regarding killing it in al-Muhit: they said: the white snake that walks straight should not be killed, because it is a jinn, due to his saying: "Kill the one with two streaks and the one with a short tail, and beware of the white snake, for it is from the jinn." End. And if he sees a snake outside prayer and doubts whether it is a jinn, he says to it: clear the path of the Muslims and fear Allah and move on; if it moves on, fine, otherwise he leaves it. And al-Tahawi said: there is no harm in killing all due to the covenant we narrated. End. And it is said: he warns it; if it refuses, he kills it. These are three sayings, and the better view is to refrain out of fear of harm; because if it refuses to move on, it intends harm, so he leaves it to avoid it. And there is no killing of a scorpion, if the worshipper fears their harm, i.e., the snake and the scorpion, and even if he kills them with multiple strikes and turning away from the qibla in the apparent view. We restricted it to fear of harm because of what was said in al-Bahr from al-Nihaya from al-Jami' al-Saghir al-Burhani: it is only permissible to kill them in prayer if they pass between his hands and he fears they will harm him, otherwise it is disliked. End. And because of what was said in al-Bazzaziyya: killing a snake with one or multiple strikes, if he fears its harm, does not invalidate and is not disliked in the apparent view, and when safe it is disliked. End. Due to his saying: "Kill the two black ones in prayer: the snake and the scorpion" narrated by the authors of the four Sunan, al-Tirmidhi said it is a sahih hadith, and in its generality it includes the need for much action. And it is said: it invalidates if strikes are many, like treating a passerby if he does much, even though he is commanded to do it. We said: in this there is another matter: the harm leading to destruction of life by their sting, and it became like walking after a precedent hadath, and drawing water from a well. End. And in al-Sub'iyyat of Abu al-Layth: seven things which if the worshiper sees, there is no harm in killing them: the snake, the scorpion, the gecko, the wasp, the tick, the flea, and the louse. Similarly in Majma' al-Riwayat. End. I say: and on this are added the mosquito, the gnat, and harmful ants that bite, and the like. End. And we have stated that taking and killing a louse in prayer is disliked according to Imam, and he said: burying it in it is more beloved than killing it. And Muhammad said contrary to that, and Abu Yusuf said it is disliked. And the author of al-Bahr said: perhaps Imam only chose burying the louse because of the cleanliness from getting its blood on the hand or garment in this state, even if it is pardoned. End. I say: and it is stated explicitly in Sharh al-Munyah: burying it is more beloved if possible, because in killing it there is creating impurity according to the view of al-Shafi'i, because its shell is impure, and as long as it is alive it is pure, so by not killing it one avoids the disagreement, lest he carry the impure that prevents according to some imams, or throw it in the mosque, so it was more beloved. And the offensiveness and dislike narrated from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf are about taking it intentionally without excuse. End.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah discusses the ruling on killing snakes and scorpions during prayer. The author begins with the ruling: if a worshiper fears harm from a snake or scorpion, it is permissible to kill them even with multiple strikes and even if one turns away from the qibla. This is the apparent (zahir) position. The reasoning is that the command to kill these creatures in the hadith overrides the prohibition of extraneous actions in prayer. The hadith cited is the Prophet's ﷺ command: 'Kill the two black ones in prayer: the snake and the scorpion.' This is a sound hadith narrated by the four sunan compilers. The commentator then addresses a potential objection: that multiple strikes may invalidate the prayer, similar to treating a passerby with many actions. He refutes this by noting that the harm from the creature's sting can lead to death, which is a greater harm, analogous to walking after an impurity or drawing water from a well out of necessity. The passage then discusses the different types of snakes: the white snake (jinniyya) and the black snake (non-jinniyya). There is an intra-Hanafi difference: some scholars say the white snake should not be killed because it is a jinn that has a covenant with the Prophet ﷺ not to harm Muslims. The preferred view is to refrain from killing it out of fear of harm. The author also mentions the view of al-Tahawi who permits killing all snakes based on another covenant. The passage concludes with a list of seven creatures that may be killed in prayer without dislike, and adds others like mosquitoes and ants. There is also a discussion about killing lice: Imam Abu Hanifa prefers burying it over killing it to avoid impurity, while Imam Muhammad allows it and Imam Abu Yusuf dislikes it. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is to bury it if possible, to avoid the differing opinions of other imams.

Key Terms
حية (hayyah): Snake; includes both jinniyya (white) and non-jinniyya (black) types.
عقرب (aqrab): Scorpion; treated similarly to snakes in terms of permissibility of killing in prayer when fearing harm.
الأظهر (al-azhar): The apparent or more evident position within the Hanafi school, often the mufta bihi.
قمل (qaml): Louse; a small insect that may appear on the body or clothes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) regarding killing the white snake in prayer?
A) It is obligatory.
B) It is permissible without dislike.
C) It is better to leave it.
D) It invalidates prayer.

Key Takeaway
The white snake has special consideration due to its jinn nature; the preferred Hanafi view is to refrain from killing it in prayer, while for lice, burying is more beloved than killing.

Permissible Actions During Prayer: Dusting Clothes, Wiping Forehead, and Looking Around
Rulings on minor permissible actions during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling (hukm) for three minor actions during salah: dusting clothes, wiping forehead, and glancing sideways, and identify the conditions under which they are permissible or disliked.

Core Idea
Minor actions that don't invalidate the prayer are permissible if needed, disliked without need.

In this passage, the commentator explains three actions that are often a concern for worshippers: shaking dust off one's garment, wiping sweat or grass from the forehead, and looking around without turning the head. Understanding when these are allowed helps maintain focus (khushu') while not obsessing over minor movements. The rulings are derived from the principle that necessity permits small actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify each action and its basic ruling
Read the passage and list the three actions: 1) nafd al-thawb (shaking garment), 2) masḥ al-jabha (wiping forehead), 3) al-nazar bi-mu'akhkhar al-'ayn (looking with the corner of the eye). Each is described as 'lā ba'sa' (no harm), indicating permissibility (mubāḥ).
These are not pillars or obligations; they are allowances.
2
Note the timing condition for wiping the forehead
The passage explicitly distinguishes between wiping after finishing the prayer and before finishing. After finishing is unconditionally allowed. Before finishing, it is only allowed if the dust causes harm or distracts the person from prayer.
The phrase 'law ḍarrahū aw shaghalahū `ani al-ṣalāt' sets the condition.
3
Understand the ruling on glancing
Looking with the corner of the eye (without turning the face) is permissible. This does not break the prayer because it is not considered turning away from the qibla. However, it may be better to avoid it without need.
The key phrase is 'min ghayri taḥwīl al-wajh' (without turning the face).
4
Relate to the principle of minor actions
These rulings fit the Hanafi principle that small amounts of extra movement (ʿamal qalīl) do not invalidate ṣalāh. Necessity (ḥarāja) expands the allowance, while without need such actions may be makrūh tanzīhan.
Compare with larger movements that break the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بنفض ثوبه كيلا يلتصق بجسده في الركوع، ولا بأس بمسح جبهته من التراب، أو الحشيش، بعد الفراغ من الصلاة، ولا قبل الفراغ إذا ضره، أو شغله عن الصلاة، ولا بالنظر بموق عينيه، من غير تحويل الوجه .
And there is no harm in shaking his garment so that it does not stick to his body during ruku, and there is no harm in wiping his forehead from dust or grass after finishing the prayer, and not before finishing if it harms him or distracts him from the prayer, and there is no harm in looking with the corners of his eyes without turning his face.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage from the commentary lists three permissible actions during prayer: First, dusting one's garment to prevent it from sticking to the body during bowing (ruku), which is allowed with a small action. Second, wiping dust or grass from the forehead after finishing the prayer is permitted without dislike. Before finishing, it is only allowed if the dust causes harm or distraction; otherwise it is disliked in the middle of prayer but not before the tashahhud and salam. Some scholars distinguish between the last rak'ah and earlier ones. Third, looking with the eyes (i.e., glancing) to the right or left without turning the face is permissible, though it is better to avoid it without need. These rulings are based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the principle that minor actions do not invalidate prayer.

Key Terms
نفض الثوب (nafd al-thawb): Shaking or dusting one's garment to remove dust or prevent it from sticking.
مسح الجبهة (masḥ al-jabhah): Wiping the forehead to remove dust or grass after prostration.
النظر بمؤخر العين (al-nazar bi-mu'akhkhar al-'ayn): Looking with the corner of the eye without turning the head, i.e., glancing sideways.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it permissible to wipe dust from the forehead during prayer according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) Only after finishing the prayer.
B) At any time during the prayer.
C) Before finishing if it causes harm or distraction.
D) Only if the dust is from the masjid floor.

Key Takeaway
Three minor actions during salah—dusting clothes, wiping forehead, and glancing sideways—are permissible when needed, with the wiping before finishing conditional on genuine harm or distraction.

Preference for Praying on Earth Over Carpets
Ruling on prayer surface validity and preference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer surfaces, identify the best surface, and explain the evidence from the hadith and the story of Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Prayer on carpets is valid, but earth or plant mats are better for humility and following the hadith.

This passage from Nur al-Idah clarifies the ruling on prayer surfaces. While praying on carpets is permissible, the superior choice is earth or natural plant materials. The text includes a hadith and a story of Imam Abu Hanifa to illustrate the principle, along with a reference to the Maliki school's different view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling on prayer surfaces
Note the phrase 'ولا بأس' indicating permissibility (mubah). Prayer on carpets, spreads, and felts is valid.
The default ruling is mubah; no prohibition.
2
Locate the superior choice
The text says 'والأفضل الصلاة على الأرض أو على ما تنبته' meaning the best is earth or what grows from it.
The word 'أفضل' indicates recommendation, not obligation.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith states: 'Psalm on what the earth produces is better than prayer on what does not produce it.' This is the evidence for preference.
The hadith is zanni in transmission and meaning, supporting recommendation.
4
Analyze the story of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa prostrated on a rag to protect from heat; when questioned, he affirmed its permissibility.
This shows barriers are allowed if needed, and knowledge is sought from scholars.
5
Connect to Maliki ikhtilaf
Choosing earth avoids the Maliki view that dislikes prostration on animal-based materials (wool, cotton, linen).
Departing from a hated disagreement is virtuous.

And there is no harm in praying on carpets, spread sheets, and felts; and the best is to pray on the earth or what it produces. And there is no harm in repeating a surah in the two rak'ahs of nafl. The etiquette of looking at the desired place, as previously. (And there is no harm in praying on carpets, spread sheets, and felts) if the volume of the ground is felt, as previously. And there is no harm in placing a rag in front of him on which he prostrates and protects himself from heat and the like, because there is nothing in it that necessitates dislike. And from Abu Hanifa that he did that, and a man passed by him and said: O Sheikh, do not do this, for it is disliked. So Abu Hanifa said: Where are you from? He said: From Khwarazm. He said: Allahu Akbar! (meaning) the takbir came from behind, i.e., from the other row, i.e., it is the opposite; meaning: knowledge of the Sharia is carried from here to Khwarazm, not from Khwarazm to here. Then he said: Is there grass in your mosque? He said: Yes. He said: Is prostration permissible on grass but not on the rag? Like that in al-Tajnis. And the best is to pray on the ground without a barrier, or on what the earth produces. He said in al-Tajnis: Prayer on grass and mats is better than prayer on the carpet, because it came in the hadith: 'Prayer on what the earth produces is better than prayer on what does not produce.' And for this reason, our Mashayikh chose grass and mats in the mosque, and not the carpet, because it is closer to humility, and it is a departure from the view of Imam Malik, for he dislikes prostrating on things like wool, cotton, or linen, so it is better. Like that in Sharh al-Munyah.

Commentary
This passage addresses the material on which prayer is performed. The basic ruling is that prayer is valid on carpets, mats, and felt (permissible). However, the superior choice is to pray directly on earth or on natural plant materials like grass and mats. A story about Imam Abu Hanifa demonstrates that even using a cloth for prostration is permissible, contrary to a man from Khwarazm who claimed it disliked. The hadith quoted supports the preference for earth. Additionally, the passage notes that this avoids the disagreement with Imam Malik who dislikes prostration on animal-derived materials.

Key Terms
الفُرُش (al-furush): Carpets or floor coverings.
الأفضل (al-afdal): The best or superior (choice).
الحشيش (al-hashish): Grass or dry plant material used as a prayer mat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Prayer on carpets is valid, but the best is to prostrate on earth or what grows from it for humility and following prophetic guidance.

Repeating a Surah in Nafl Prayer
Ruling on repeating the same surah in voluntary prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeating a surah in nafl prayer and cite the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
In nafl prayer, repeating a surah is allowed because the door of nafl is wider.

A common question among those who pray voluntary prayers is whether it is permissible to recite the same surah in both rak'ahs of a nafl prayer. This lesson addresses that question based on the Hanafi school. We will examine the ruling and its proof from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is repeating a surah in the two rak'ahs of a nafl prayer. The ruling is that there is no harm (i.e., it is permissible).
The ruling is mubah, not wajib or haram.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites a hadith: the Prophet stood reciting a single verse repeatedly in his tahajjud prayer. This is an evidence from the Sunnah.
The hadith is ahad, providing zanni proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of repeating a verse shows that repetition is allowed in nafl. Since tahajjud is a type of nafl, the ruling extends to all nafl prayers.
The broader principle 'babul nafl awsa' (the door of nafl is wider) supports leniency.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant disagreement among the schools on this point; it is unanimously permissible.
The text indicates it is agreed upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بتكرار السورة في الركعتين من النقل؛ لأن باب النفل أوسع، وقد ورد أنَّهُ قَامَ بِآيَةٍ وَاحِدَة يُكَرِّرُهَا فِي تَهَجده، كما قدمناه )

Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This short passage addresses a common question: can one recite the same surah in both rak'ahs of a nafl prayer? The answer is yes, there is no harm. The reason given is that the category of nafl (supererogatory) is more spacious and less restricted than fard. Evidence is drawn from the Prophet's practice of repeating a single verse in tahajjud prayer, as narrated.

Key Terms
النقل (al-naql): Voluntary prayer (nafl).
التهجد (al-tahajjud): Night prayer; a type of nafl.

Repeating a surah in nafl prayer is permissible and supported by the Prophet's practice and the principle that nafl has a wider scope.
