Forgetting Qunut in Witr: Remembering in Ruku'
Ruling on forgetting qunut in witr and remembering after entering ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct ruling when qunut is forgotten in witr and remembered in ruku', and explain why sajda al-sahw is required.

Core Idea
If you forget qunut in witr and remember in ruku', do not perform it; do sajda al-sahw.

When performing witr prayer, the qunut supplication is a wajib (obligatory) element. But what happens if you forget it and only remember after you have already gone into ruku'? This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies that the correct course is not to perform the qunut belatedly, but rather to compensate with the prostration of forgetfulness (sajda al-sahw). We will analyze the reasoning and the special case if someone mistakenly does perform qunut after ruku'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the qunut in witr, which is wajib in the Hanafi school. The passage addresses the scenario where it is forgotten and remembered after entering ruku'.
Qunut is specific to the third rak'ah of witr in the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the prohibition of performing qunut late
The text states 'لا يقنت على الصحيح' (he does not perform qunut on the correct view), meaning that once you have moved past the standing position and entered ruku', the proper place for qunut has passed.
Performing it in ruku' or after rising would be an incorrect placement (takhyeel).
3
Apply the rule of wajib omission
Since qunut is wajib, omitting it requires compensation via sajda al-sahw. The passage confirms 'ويسجد للسهو' (and he performs sajda al-sahw).
In Hanafi fiqh, omitting a wajib in prayer necessitates sajda al-sahw.
4
Note the case of performing qunut after ruku'
If after raising from ruku' the person performs qunut, they do not repeat the ruku' ('لا يعد الركوع'). The prayer remains valid, but sajda al-sahw is still required because the qunut was moved from its original place.
The ruku' itself is not invalidated; the error is in timing.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position is: if qunut is forgotten and remembered in ruku' or after, do not perform it, and do sajda al-sahw. If performed after ruku', the prayer is not invalidated, but sajda al-sahw remains wajib.
This is supported by al-Kamal and Qadi Khan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا نسي القُنوت في) ثالثة ( الوِتْرِ، وَتَذَكَّرَهُ في الركوع أوِ الرفع منه)، أي: الركوع ( لا يَقْنُتُ على الصحيح، لا في الركوع الذي تذكر فيه، ولا بـعـد الـرفـع منه، ويسجد للسهو، (ولو قنَتَ بعد رفع رأسهِ منَ الرّكوعِ، لا يُعيد الركوع) كما قالــه الـكـمـال عـن قاضي خان»، فإن عاد إلى القيام وقنت، ولم يعد الركوع لم تفسد صلاته؛ لأن ركوعــه قـائـم لم يرتفـض ويسجد للسهو، لزوال القنوتِ عن محله الأصلي. فسجود السهو واجب عليه، قنت بعد الرفع أو لم يقنت؛ لأنه إن قنت فقد قدم وأخر، وإن لم يقنت فلتركه الواجب أصلاً.
And if he forgets the qunut in the third (of witr) and remembers it while bowing or after rising from it, meaning bowing, he does not perform qunut according to the correct view, neither in the bowing in which he remembered it nor after rising from it, and he performs sajda al-sahw. And if he performed qunut after raising his head from bowing, he does not repeat the bowing, as al-Kamal said from Qadi Khan. If he returns to standing and performs qunut and does not repeat the bowing, his prayer is not invalid because his bowing remains intact. And he performs sajda al-sahw because the qunut left its original place. So sajda al-sahw is obligatory upon him, whether he performed qunut after rising or not, because if he performed it, he advanced and delayed, and if he did not perform it, he left an obligatory act entirely.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with reasoning regarding forgetting the qunut in witr. The correct view is that if one remembers the qunut while in ruku' or after rising, he should not perform it, as its proper place has passed. He must perform sajda al-sahw for omitting a wajib. If he erroneously performs qunut after rising from ruku', he does not repeat the ruku'; his prayer remains valid, but he still must perform sajda al-sahw because he has altered the sequence of the prayer.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): A supplication recited in the third rak'ah of witr after ruku'.
سهو السهو (sajda al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for errors in prayer, such as omitting a wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person forgets the qunut in witr and remembers while in ruku', what is the correct action according to the Hanafi school?
A) Stand up and perform the qunut after ruku'
B) Perform the qunut in the ruku' position
C) Do not perform the qunut and perform sajda al-sahw after the prayer
D) Repeat the entire rak'ah

Key Takeaway
Forgetting qunut in witr and remembering in ruku' means you do not perform qunut; you must perform sajda al-sahw for omitting a wajib.
